# f5xc_http_loadbalancer (Resource)

Manages a HTTPLoadBalancer resource in F5 Distributed Cloud for load balancing HTTP/HTTPS traffic with advanced routing and security.

~> **Note** For more information about this resource, please refer to the [F5 XC API Documentation](https://docs.cloud.f5.com/docs/api/).

## Example Usage

```terraform
# Http Loadbalancer Resource Example
# Manages a HTTPLoadBalancer resource in F5 Distributed Cloud for load balancing HTTP/HTTPS traffic with advanced routing and security.

# Basic Http Loadbalancer configuration
resource "f5xc_http_loadbalancer" "example" {
  name      = "example-http-loadbalancer"
  namespace = "system"

  labels = {
    environment = "production"
    managed_by  = "terraform"
  }

  annotations = {
    "owner" = "platform-team"
  }

  # HTTP Load Balancer specific configuration
  domains = ["app.example.com"]

  # Advertise on public internet
  advertise_on_internet {
    default_vip {}
  }

  # Default origin server
  default_route_pools {
    pool {
      name      = "example-origin-pool"
      namespace = "system"
    }
    weight   = 1
    priority = 1
  }

  # Enable HTTP to HTTPS redirect
  http {
    dns_volterra_managed = true
  }

  # Disable rate limiting by default
  disable_rate_limit {}

  # No WAF by default
  disable_waf {}
}
```

- `name` (String) Name of the HTTPLoadBalancer. Must be unique within the namespace.
- `namespace` (String) Namespace where the HTTPLoadBalancer will be created.

### Nested Schema for `active_service_policies`

Optional:

- `policies` (Block List) Policies. Service Policies is a sequential engine where policies (and rules within the policy) are evaluated one after the other. It's important to define the correct order (policies evaluated from top to bottom in the list) for service policies, to get the intended result. For each request, its characteristics are evaluated based on the match criteria in each service policy starting at the top. If there is a match in the current policy, then the policy takes effect, and no more policies are ... (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--active_service_policies--policies))

<a id="nestedblock--advertise_custom--advertise_where--virtual_site"></a>
### Nested Schema for `advertise_custom.advertise_where.virtual_site`

Optional:

- `network` (String) Site Network. This defines network types to be used on site All inside and outside networks. All inside and outside networks with internet VIP support. All inside networks. All outside networks. All outside networks with internet VIP support. vK8s service network. - SITE_NETWORK_IP_FABRIC: VER IP Fabric network for the site This Virtual network type is used for exposing virtual host on IP Fabric network on the VER site or for endpoint in IP Fabric network. Possible values are `SITE_NETWORK_INSIDE_AND_OUTSIDE`, `SITE_NETWORK_INSIDE`, `SITE_NETWORK_OUTSIDE`, `SITE_NETWORK_SERVICE`, `SITE_NETWORK_OUTSIDE_WITH_INTERNET_VIP`, `SITE_NETWORK_INSIDE_AND_OUTSIDE_WITH_INTERNET_VIP`, `SITE_NETWORK_IP_FABRIC`.
- `virtual_site` (Block, Optional) Object reference. This type establishes a direct reference from one object(the referrer) to another(the referred). Such a reference is in form of tenant/namespace/name (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--advertise_custom--advertise_where--virtual_site--virtual_site))

<a id="nestedblock--advertise_custom--advertise_where--virtual_site--virtual_site"></a>

Optional:

- `ip` (String) IP Address. Use given IP address as VIP on the site
- `network` (String) Site Network. This defines network types to be used on virtual-site with specified VIP All outside networks. All inside networks. Possible values are `SITE_NETWORK_SPECIFIED_VIP_OUTSIDE`, `SITE_NETWORK_SPECIFIED_VIP_INSIDE`.
- `virtual_site` (Block, Optional) Object reference. This type establishes a direct reference from one object(the referrer) to another(the referred). Such a reference is in form of tenant/namespace/name (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--advertise_custom--advertise_where--virtual_site_with_vip--virtual_site))

<a id="nestedblock--advertise_on_public"></a>
### Nested Schema for `advertise_on_public`

Optional:

- `public_ip` (Block, Optional) Object reference. This type establishes a direct reference from one object(the referrer) to another(the referred). Such a reference is in form of tenant/namespace/name (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--advertise_on_public--public_ip))

<a id="nestedblock--advertise_on_public--public_ip"></a>
### Nested Schema for `advertise_on_public.public_ip`

Optional:

- `name` (String) Name. When a configuration object(e.g. virtual_host) refers to another(e.g route) then name will hold the referred object's(e.g. route's) name.
- `namespace` (String) Namespace. When a configuration object(e.g. virtual_host) refers to another(e.g route) then namespace will hold the referred object's(e.g. route's) namespace.
- `tenant` (String) Tenant. When a configuration object(e.g. virtual_host) refers to another(e.g route) then tenant will hold the referred object's(e.g. route's) tenant.

<a id="nestedblock--api_protection_rules"></a>
### Nested Schema for `api_protection_rules`

Optional:

- `api_endpoint_rules` (Block List) API Endpoints. This category defines specific rules per API endpoints. If request matches any of these rules, skipping second category rules. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_protection_rules--api_endpoint_rules))
- `api_groups_rules` (Block List) Server URLs and API Groups. This category includes rules per API group or Server URL. For API groups, refer to API Definition which includes API groups derived from uploaded swaggers. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_protection_rules--api_groups_rules))

<a id="nestedblock--api_protection_rules--api_endpoint_rules"></a>
### Nested Schema for `api_protection_rules.api_endpoint_rules`

Optional:

- `action` (Block, Optional) API Protection Rule Action. The action to take if the input request matches the rule. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_protection_rules--api_endpoint_rules--action))
- `any_domain` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_protection_rules--api_endpoint_rules--any_domain))
- `api_endpoint_method` (Block, Optional) HTTP Method Matcher. A http method matcher specifies a list of methods to match an input HTTP method. The match is considered successful if the input method is a member of the list. The result of the match based on the method list is inverted if invert_matcher is true. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_protection_rules--api_endpoint_rules--api_endpoint_method))
- `api_endpoint_path` (String) API Endpoint. The endpoint (path) of the request.
- `client_matcher` (Block, Optional) Client Matcher. Client conditions for matching a rule (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_protection_rules--api_endpoint_rules--client_matcher))
- `metadata` (Block, Optional) Message Metadata. MessageMetaType is metadata (common attributes) of a message that only certain messages have. This information is propagated to the metadata of a child object that gets created from the containing message during view processing. The information in this type can be specified by user during create and replace APIs. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_protection_rules--api_endpoint_rules--metadata))
- `request_matcher` (Block, Optional) Request Matcher. Request conditions for matching a rule (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_protection_rules--api_endpoint_rules--request_matcher))
- `specific_domain` (String) Specific Domain. The rule will apply for a specific domain. For example: api.example.com

<a id="nestedblock--api_protection_rules--api_endpoint_rules--action"></a>
### Nested Schema for `api_protection_rules.api_endpoint_rules.action`

Optional:

- `allow` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_protection_rules--api_endpoint_rules--action--allow))
- `deny` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_protection_rules--api_endpoint_rules--action--deny))

<a id="nestedblock--api_protection_rules--api_endpoint_rules--api_endpoint_method"></a>
### Nested Schema for `api_protection_rules.api_endpoint_rules.api_endpoint_method`

Optional:

- `invert_matcher` (Boolean) Invert Method Matcher. Invert the match result.
- `methods` (List of String) Method List. List of methods values to match against.


<a id="nestedblock--api_protection_rules--api_endpoint_rules--client_matcher"></a>
### Nested Schema for `api_protection_rules.api_endpoint_rules.client_matcher`

Optional:

- `any_client` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_protection_rules--api_endpoint_rules--client_matcher--any_client))
- `any_ip` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_protection_rules--api_endpoint_rules--client_matcher--any_ip))
- `asn_list` (Block, Optional) ASN Match List. An unordered set of RFC 6793 defined 4-byte AS numbers that can be used to create allow or deny lists for use in network policy or service policy. It can be used to create the allow list only for DNS Load Balancer. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_protection_rules--api_endpoint_rules--client_matcher--asn_list))
- `asn_matcher` (Block, Optional) ASN Matcher. Match any AS number contained in the list of bgp_asn_sets. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_protection_rules--api_endpoint_rules--client_matcher--asn_matcher))
- `client_selector` (Block, Optional) Label Selector. This type can be used to establish a 'selector reference' from one object(called selector) to a set of other objects(called selectees) based on the value of expresssions. A label selector is a label query over a set of resources. An empty label selector matches all objects. A null label selector matches no objects. Label selector is immutable. expressions is a list of strings of label selection expression. Each string has ',' separated values which are 'AND' and all strings ar... (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_protection_rules--api_endpoint_rules--client_matcher--client_selector))
- `ip_matcher` (Block, Optional) IP Prefix Matcher. Match any ip prefix contained in the list of ip_prefix_sets. The result of the match is inverted if invert_matcher is true. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_protection_rules--api_endpoint_rules--client_matcher--ip_matcher))
- `ip_prefix_list` (Block, Optional) IP Prefix Match List. List of IP Prefix strings to match against. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_protection_rules--api_endpoint_rules--client_matcher--ip_prefix_list))
- `ip_threat_category_list` (Block, Optional) IP Threat Category List Type. List of ip threat categories (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_protection_rules--api_endpoint_rules--client_matcher--ip_threat_category_list))
- `tls_fingerprint_matcher` (Block, Optional) TLS Fingerprint Matcher. A TLS fingerprint matcher specifies multiple criteria for matching a TLS fingerprint. The set of supported positve match criteria includes a list of known classes of TLS fingerprints and a list of exact values. The match is considered successful if either of these positive criteria are satisfied and the input fingerprint is not one of the excluded values. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_protection_rules--api_endpoint_rules--client_matcher--tls_fingerprint_matcher))

<a id="nestedblock--api_protection_rules--api_endpoint_rules--client_matcher--any_client"></a>

<a id="nestedblock--api_protection_rules--api_endpoint_rules--metadata"></a>
### Nested Schema for `api_protection_rules.api_endpoint_rules.metadata`

Optional:

- `description` (String) Description. Human readable description.
- `name` (String) Name. This is the name of the message. The value of name has to follow DNS-1035 format.


<a id="nestedblock--api_protection_rules--api_endpoint_rules--request_matcher"></a>
### Nested Schema for `api_protection_rules.api_endpoint_rules.request_matcher`

Optional:

- `cookie_matchers` (Block List) Cookie Matchers. A list of predicates for all cookies that need to be matched. The criteria for matching each cookie is described in individual instances of CookieMatcherType. The actual cookie values are extracted from the request API as a list of strings for each cookie name. Note that all specified cookie matcher predicates must evaluate to true. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_protection_rules--api_endpoint_rules--request_matcher--cookie_matchers))
- `headers` (Block List) HTTP Headers. A list of predicates for various HTTP headers that need to match. The criteria for matching each HTTP header are described in individual HeaderMatcherType instances. The actual HTTP header values are extracted from the request API as a list of strings for each HTTP header type. Note that all specified header predicates must evaluate to true. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_protection_rules--api_endpoint_rules--request_matcher--headers))
- `jwt_claims` (Block List) JWT Claims. A list of predicates for various JWT claims that need to match. The criteria for matching each JWT claim are described in individual JWTClaimMatcherType instances. The actual JWT claims values are extracted from the JWT payload as a list of strings. Note that all specified JWT claim predicates must evaluate to true. Note that this feature only works on LBs with JWT Validation feature enabled. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_protection_rules--api_endpoint_rules--request_matcher--jwt_claims))
- `query_params` (Block List) HTTP Query Parameters. A list of predicates for all query parameters that need to be matched. The criteria for matching each query parameter are described in individual instances of QueryParameterMatcherType. The actual query parameter values are extracted from the request API as a list of strings for each query parameter name. Note that all specified query parameter predicates must evaluate to true. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_protection_rules--api_endpoint_rules--request_matcher--query_params))

<a id="nestedblock--api_protection_rules--api_endpoint_rules--request_matcher--cookie_matchers"></a>
### Nested Schema for `api_protection_rules.api_endpoint_rules.request_matcher.cookie_matchers`

- `api_group` (String) API Group. API groups derived from API Definition swaggers. For example oas-all-operations including all paths and methods from the swaggers, oas-base-urls covering all requests under base-paths from the swaggers. Custom groups can be created if user tags paths or operations with 'x-volterra-api-group' extensions inside swaggers.
- `base_path` (String) Base Path. Prefix of the request path. For example: /v1
- `client_matcher` (Block, Optional) Client Matcher. Client conditions for matching a rule (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_protection_rules--api_groups_rules--client_matcher))
- `metadata` (Block, Optional) Message Metadata. MessageMetaType is metadata (common attributes) of a message that only certain messages have. This information is propagated to the metadata of a child object that gets created from the containing message during view processing. The information in this type can be specified by user during create and replace APIs. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_protection_rules--api_groups_rules--metadata))
- `request_matcher` (Block, Optional) Request Matcher. Request conditions for matching a rule (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_protection_rules--api_groups_rules--request_matcher))
- `specific_domain` (String) Specific Domain. The rule will apply for a specific domain. For example: api.example.com

<a id="nestedblock--api_protection_rules--api_groups_rules--request_matcher--query_params"></a>
### Nested Schema for `api_protection_rules.api_groups_rules.request_matcher.query_params`





<a id="nestedblock--api_rate_limit"></a>
### Nested Schema for `api_rate_limit`

Optional:

- `api_endpoint_rules` (Block List) API Endpoints. Sets of rules for a specific endpoints. Order is matter as it uses first match policy. For creating rule that contain a whole domain or group of endpoints, please use the server URL rules above. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_rate_limit--api_endpoint_rules))
- `bypass_rate_limiting_rules` (Block, Optional) Bypass Rate Limiting. This category defines rules per URL or API group. If request matches any of these rules, skip Rate Limiting. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_rate_limit--bypass_rate_limiting_rules))
- `custom_ip_allowed_list` (Block, Optional) Custom IP Allowed List. IP Allowed list using existing ip_prefix_set objects (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_rate_limit--custom_ip_allowed_list))
- `ip_allowed_list` (Block, Optional) IPv4 Prefix List. x-example: '192.168.20.0/24' List of IPv4 prefixes that represent an endpoint (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_rate_limit--ip_allowed_list))
- `no_ip_allowed_list` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_rate_limit--no_ip_allowed_list))
- `server_url_rules` (Block List) Server URLs. Set of rules for entire domain or base path that contain multiple endpoints. Order is matter as it uses first match policy. For matching also specific endpoints you can use the API endpoint rules set bellow. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_rate_limit--server_url_rules))

<a id="nestedblock--api_rate_limit--api_endpoint_rules"></a>
### Nested Schema for `api_rate_limit.api_endpoint_rules`

Optional:

- `any_domain` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_rate_limit--api_endpoint_rules--any_domain))
- `api_endpoint_method` (Block, Optional) HTTP Method Matcher. A http method matcher specifies a list of methods to match an input HTTP method. The match is considered successful if the input method is a member of the list. The result of the match based on the method list is inverted if invert_matcher is true. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_rate_limit--api_endpoint_rules--api_endpoint_method))
- `api_endpoint_path` (String) API Endpoint. The endpoint (path) of the request.
- `client_matcher` (Block, Optional) Client Matcher. Client conditions for matching a rule (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_rate_limit--api_endpoint_rules--client_matcher))
- `inline_rate_limiter` (Block, Optional) InlineRateLimiter. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_rate_limit--api_endpoint_rules--inline_rate_limiter))
- `ref_rate_limiter` (Block, Optional) Object reference. This type establishes a direct reference from one object(the referrer) to another(the referred). Such a reference is in form of tenant/namespace/name (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_rate_limit--api_endpoint_rules--ref_rate_limiter))
- `request_matcher` (Block, Optional) Request Matcher. Request conditions for matching a rule (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_rate_limit--api_endpoint_rules--request_matcher))
- `specific_domain` (String) Specific Domain. The rule will apply for a specific domain.

<a id="nestedblock--api_rate_limit--api_endpoint_rules--any_domain"></a>
### Nested Schema for `api_rate_limit.api_endpoint_rules.any_domain`


<a id="nestedblock--api_rate_limit--api_endpoint_rules--api_endpoint_method"></a>
### Nested Schema for `api_rate_limit.api_endpoint_rules.api_endpoint_method`

Optional:

- `invert_matcher` (Boolean) Invert Method Matcher. Invert the match result.
- `methods` (List of String) Method List. List of methods values to match against.


<a id="nestedblock--api_rate_limit--api_endpoint_rules--client_matcher"></a>
### Nested Schema for `api_rate_limit.api_endpoint_rules.client_matcher`

Optional:

- `any_client` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_rate_limit--api_endpoint_rules--client_matcher--any_client))
- `any_ip` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_rate_limit--api_endpoint_rules--client_matcher--any_ip))
- `asn_list` (Block, Optional) ASN Match List. An unordered set of RFC 6793 defined 4-byte AS numbers that can be used to create allow or deny lists for use in network policy or service policy. It can be used to create the allow list only for DNS Load Balancer. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_rate_limit--api_endpoint_rules--client_matcher--asn_list))
- `asn_matcher` (Block, Optional) ASN Matcher. Match any AS number contained in the list of bgp_asn_sets. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_rate_limit--api_endpoint_rules--client_matcher--asn_matcher))
- `client_selector` (Block, Optional) Label Selector. This type can be used to establish a 'selector reference' from one object(called selector) to a set of other objects(called selectees) based on the value of expresssions. A label selector is a label query over a set of resources. An empty label selector matches all objects. A null label selector matches no objects. Label selector is immutable. expressions is a list of strings of label selection expression. Each string has ',' separated values which are 'AND' and all strings ar... (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_rate_limit--api_endpoint_rules--client_matcher--client_selector))
- `ip_matcher` (Block, Optional) IP Prefix Matcher. Match any ip prefix contained in the list of ip_prefix_sets. The result of the match is inverted if invert_matcher is true. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_rate_limit--api_endpoint_rules--client_matcher--ip_matcher))
- `ip_prefix_list` (Block, Optional) IP Prefix Match List. List of IP Prefix strings to match against. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_rate_limit--api_endpoint_rules--client_matcher--ip_prefix_list))
- `ip_threat_category_list` (Block, Optional) IP Threat Category List Type. List of ip threat categories (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_rate_limit--api_endpoint_rules--client_matcher--ip_threat_category_list))
- `tls_fingerprint_matcher` (Block, Optional) TLS Fingerprint Matcher. A TLS fingerprint matcher specifies multiple criteria for matching a TLS fingerprint. The set of supported positve match criteria includes a list of known classes of TLS fingerprints and a list of exact values. The match is considered successful if either of these positive criteria are satisfied and the input fingerprint is not one of the excluded values. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_rate_limit--api_endpoint_rules--client_matcher--tls_fingerprint_matcher))

<a id="nestedblock--api_rate_limit--api_endpoint_rules--client_matcher--any_client"></a>

<a id="nestedblock--api_rate_limit--api_endpoint_rules--inline_rate_limiter"></a>
### Nested Schema for `api_rate_limit.api_endpoint_rules.inline_rate_limiter`

Optional:

- `ref_user_id` (Block, Optional) Object reference. This type establishes a direct reference from one object(the referrer) to another(the referred). Such a reference is in form of tenant/namespace/name (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_rate_limit--api_endpoint_rules--inline_rate_limiter--ref_user_id))
- `threshold` (Number) Threshold. The total number of allowed requests for 1 unit (e.g. SECOND/MINUTE/HOUR etc.) of the specified period.
- `unit` (String) Rate Limit Period Unit. Unit for the period per which the rate limit is applied. - SECOND: Second Rate limit period unit is seconds - MINUTE: Minute Rate limit period unit is minutes - HOUR: Hour Rate limit period unit is hours - DAY: Day Rate limit period unit is days. Possible values are `SECOND`, `MINUTE`, `HOUR`.
- `use_http_lb_user_id` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_rate_limit--api_endpoint_rules--inline_rate_limiter--use_http_lb_user_id))

<a id="nestedblock--api_rate_limit--api_endpoint_rules--ref_rate_limiter"></a>
### Nested Schema for `api_rate_limit.api_endpoint_rules.ref_rate_limiter`

Optional:

- `name` (String) Name. When a configuration object(e.g. virtual_host) refers to another(e.g route) then name will hold the referred object's(e.g. route's) name.
- `namespace` (String) Namespace. When a configuration object(e.g. virtual_host) refers to another(e.g route) then namespace will hold the referred object's(e.g. route's) namespace.
- `tenant` (String) Tenant. When a configuration object(e.g. virtual_host) refers to another(e.g route) then tenant will hold the referred object's(e.g. route's) tenant.


<a id="nestedblock--api_rate_limit--api_endpoint_rules--request_matcher"></a>
### Nested Schema for `api_rate_limit.api_endpoint_rules.request_matcher`

Optional:

- `cookie_matchers` (Block List) Cookie Matchers. A list of predicates for all cookies that need to be matched. The criteria for matching each cookie is described in individual instances of CookieMatcherType. The actual cookie values are extracted from the request API as a list of strings for each cookie name. Note that all specified cookie matcher predicates must evaluate to true. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_rate_limit--api_endpoint_rules--request_matcher--cookie_matchers))
- `headers` (Block List) HTTP Headers. A list of predicates for various HTTP headers that need to match. The criteria for matching each HTTP header are described in individual HeaderMatcherType instances. The actual HTTP header values are extracted from the request API as a list of strings for each HTTP header type. Note that all specified header predicates must evaluate to true. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_rate_limit--api_endpoint_rules--request_matcher--headers))
- `jwt_claims` (Block List) JWT Claims. A list of predicates for various JWT claims that need to match. The criteria for matching each JWT claim are described in individual JWTClaimMatcherType instances. The actual JWT claims values are extracted from the JWT payload as a list of strings. Note that all specified JWT claim predicates must evaluate to true. Note that this feature only works on LBs with JWT Validation feature enabled. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_rate_limit--api_endpoint_rules--request_matcher--jwt_claims))
- `query_params` (Block List) HTTP Query Parameters. A list of predicates for all query parameters that need to be matched. The criteria for matching each query parameter are described in individual instances of QueryParameterMatcherType. The actual query parameter values are extracted from the request API as a list of strings for each query parameter name. Note that all specified query parameter predicates must evaluate to true. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_rate_limit--api_endpoint_rules--request_matcher--query_params))

<a id="nestedblock--api_rate_limit--api_endpoint_rules--request_matcher--cookie_matchers"></a>
### Nested Schema for `api_rate_limit.api_endpoint_rules.request_matcher.cookie_matchers`

### Nested Schema for `api_rate_limit.server_url_rules.ref_rate_limiter`

Optional:

- `name` (String) Name. When a configuration object(e.g. virtual_host) refers to another(e.g route) then name will hold the referred object's(e.g. route's) name.
- `namespace` (String) Namespace. When a configuration object(e.g. virtual_host) refers to another(e.g route) then namespace will hold the referred object's(e.g. route's) namespace.
- `tenant` (String) Tenant. When a configuration object(e.g. virtual_host) refers to another(e.g route) then tenant will hold the referred object's(e.g. route's) tenant.


<a id="nestedblock--api_rate_limit--server_url_rules--request_matcher"></a>
### Nested Schema for `api_rate_limit.server_url_rules.request_matcher`

Optional:

- `cookie_matchers` (Block List) Cookie Matchers. A list of predicates for all cookies that need to be matched. The criteria for matching each cookie is described in individual instances of CookieMatcherType. The actual cookie values are extracted from the request API as a list of strings for each cookie name. Note that all specified cookie matcher predicates must evaluate to true. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_rate_limit--server_url_rules--request_matcher--cookie_matchers))
- `headers` (Block List) HTTP Headers. A list of predicates for various HTTP headers that need to match. The criteria for matching each HTTP header are described in individual HeaderMatcherType instances. The actual HTTP header values are extracted from the request API as a list of strings for each HTTP header type. Note that all specified header predicates must evaluate to true. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_rate_limit--server_url_rules--request_matcher--headers))
- `jwt_claims` (Block List) JWT Claims. A list of predicates for various JWT claims that need to match. The criteria for matching each JWT claim are described in individual JWTClaimMatcherType instances. The actual JWT claims values are extracted from the JWT payload as a list of strings. Note that all specified JWT claim predicates must evaluate to true. Note that this feature only works on LBs with JWT Validation feature enabled. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_rate_limit--server_url_rules--request_matcher--jwt_claims))
- `query_params` (Block List) HTTP Query Parameters. A list of predicates for all query parameters that need to be matched. The criteria for matching each query parameter are described in individual instances of QueryParameterMatcherType. The actual query parameter values are extracted from the request API as a list of strings for each query parameter name. Note that all specified query parameter predicates must evaluate to true. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--api_rate_limit--server_url_rules--request_matcher--query_params))

<a id="nestedblock--api_rate_limit--server_url_rules--request_matcher--cookie_matchers"></a>
### Nested Schema for `api_rate_limit.server_url_rules.request_matcher.cookie_matchers`


<a id="nestedblock--api_rate_limit--server_url_rules--request_matcher--headers"></a>

### Nested Schema for `api_rate_limit.server_url_rules.request_matcher.jwt_claims`

Optional:

- `as_number` (Number) AS Number. RFC 6793 defined 4-byte AS number

- `expiration_timestamp` (String) Expiration Timestamp. The expiration_timestamp is the RFC 3339 format timestamp at which the containing rule is considered to be logically expired. The rule continues to exist in the configuration but is not applied anymore.
- `http_header` (Block, Optional) HTTP Header. Request header name and value pairs (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--blocked_clients--http_header))
- `ip_prefix` (String) IPv4 Prefix. IPv4 prefix string.

This information is propagated to the metadata of a child object that gets created from the containing message during view processing. The information in this type can be specified by user during create and replace APIs. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--blocked_clients--metadata))
- `skip_processing` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--blocked_clients--skip_processing))
- `user_identifier` (String) User Identifier. Identify user based on user identifier. User identifier value needs to be copied from security event.

<a id="nestedblock--blocked_clients--http_header--headers"></a>

Optional:

- `presence` (Boolean) Presence. If true, check for presence of header
- `regex` (String) Regex. Regex match of the header value in re2 format

- `policy` (Block, Optional) Bot Defense Policy. This defines various configuration options for Bot Defense policy. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--bot_defense--policy))
- `regional_endpoint` (String) Bot Defense Region. Defines a selection for Bot Defense region - AUTO: AUTO Automatic selection based on client IP address - US: US US region - EU: EU European Union region - ASIA: ASIA Asia region. Possible values are `AUTO`, `US`, `EU`, `ASIA`.
- `timeout` (Number) Timeout. The timeout for the inference check, in milliseconds.

<a id="nestedblock--bot_defense--policy"></a>
### Nested Schema for `bot_defense.policy`

Optional:

- `disable_js_insert` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--bot_defense--policy--disable_js_insert))
- `disable_mobile_sdk` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--bot_defense--policy--disable_mobile_sdk))
- `javascript_mode` (String) Web Client JavaScript Mode. Web Client JavaScript Mode. Bot Defense JavaScript for telemetry collection is requested asynchronously, and it is non-cacheable Bot Defense JavaScript for telemetry collection is requested asynchronously, and it is cacheable Bot Defense JavaScript for telemetry collection is requested synchronously, and it is non-cacheable Bot Defense JavaScript for telemetry collection is requested synchronously, and it is cacheable. Possible values are `ASYNC_JS_NO_CACHING`, `ASYNC_JS_CACHING`, `SYNC_JS_NO_CACHING`, `SYNC_JS_CACHING`.
- `js_download_path` (String) JavaScript Download Path. Customize Bot Defense Client JavaScript path. If not specified, default `/common.js`
- `js_insert_all_pages` (Block, Optional) Insert Bot Defense JavaScript in All Pages. Insert Bot Defense JavaScript in all pages (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--bot_defense--policy--js_insert_all_pages))
- `js_insert_all_pages_except` (Block, Optional) Insert JavaScript in All Pages with the Exceptions. Insert Bot Defense JavaScript in all pages with the exceptions (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--bot_defense--policy--js_insert_all_pages_except))
- `js_insertion_rules` (Block, Optional) JavaScript Custom Insertion Rules. This defines custom JavaScript insertion rules for Bot Defense Policy. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--bot_defense--policy--js_insertion_rules))
- `mobile_sdk_config` (Block, Optional) Mobile SDK Configuration. Mobile SDK configuration. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--bot_defense--policy--mobile_sdk_config))
- `protected_app_endpoints` (Block List) App Endpoint Type. List of protected endpoints. Limit: Approx '128 endpoints per Load Balancer (LB)' upto 4 LBs, '32 endpoints per LB' after 4 LBs. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--bot_defense--policy--protected_app_endpoints))

<a id="nestedblock--bot_defense--policy--protected_app_endpoints"></a>
### Nested Schema for `bot_defense.policy.protected_app_endpoints`

Optional:

- `allow_good_bots` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--bot_defense--policy--protected_app_endpoints--allow_good_bots))
- `any_domain` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--bot_defense--policy--protected_app_endpoints--any_domain))
- `domain` (Block, Optional) Domains. Domains names (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--bot_defense--policy--protected_app_endpoints--domain))
- `flow_label` (Block, Optional) Bot Defense Flow Label Category. Bot Defense Flow Label Category allows to associate traffic with selected category (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--bot_defense--policy--protected_app_endpoints--flow_label))
- `headers` (Block List) HTTP Headers. A list of predicates for various HTTP headers that need to match. The criteria for matching each HTTP header are described in individual HeaderMatcherType instances. The actual HTTP header values are extracted from the request API as a list of strings for each HTTP header type. Note that all specified header predicates must evaluate to true. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--bot_defense--policy--protected_app_endpoints--headers))
- `http_methods` (List of String) HTTP Methods. List of HTTP methods.
- `metadata` (Block, Optional) Message Metadata. MessageMetaType is metadata (common attributes) of a message that only certain messages have. This information is propagated to the metadata of a child object that gets created from the containing message during view processing. The information in this type can be specified by user during create and replace APIs. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--bot_defense--policy--protected_app_endpoints--metadata))
- `mitigate_good_bots` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--bot_defense--policy--protected_app_endpoints--mitigate_good_bots))
- `mitigation` (Block, Optional) Bot Mitigation Action. Modify Bot Defense behavior for a matching request. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--bot_defense--policy--protected_app_endpoints--mitigation))
- `mobile` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--bot_defense--policy--protected_app_endpoints--mobile))
- `path` (Block, Optional) Path to Match. Path match of the URI can be either be, Prefix match or exact match or regular expression match (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--bot_defense--policy--protected_app_endpoints--path))
- `protocol` (String) URL Scheme. SchemeType is used to indicate URL scheme. - BOTH: BOTH URL scheme for https:// or http://. - HTTP: HTTP URL scheme http:// only. - HTTPS: HTTPS URL scheme https:// only. Possible values are `BOTH`, `HTTP`, `HTTPS`.
- `query_params` (Block List) HTTP Query Parameters. A list of predicates for all query parameters that need to be matched. The criteria for matching each query parameter are described in individual instances of QueryParameterMatcherType. The actual query parameter values are extracted from the request API as a list of strings for each query parameter name. Note that all specified query parameter predicates must evaluate to true. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--bot_defense--policy--protected_app_endpoints--query_params))
- `undefined_flow_label` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--bot_defense--policy--protected_app_endpoints--undefined_flow_label))
- `web` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--bot_defense--policy--protected_app_endpoints--web))
- `web_mobile` (Block, Optional) Web and Mobile traffic type. Web and Mobile traffic type (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--bot_defense--policy--protected_app_endpoints--web_mobile))

<a id="nestedblock--captcha_challenge"></a>
### Nested Schema for `captcha_challenge`

Optional:

- `cookie_expiry` (Number) Cookie Expiration Period. Cookie expiration period, in seconds. An expired cookie causes the loadbalancer to issue a new challenge.
- `custom_page` (String) Custom message for Captcha Challenge. Custom message is of type uri_ref. Currently supported URL schemes is string:///. For string:/// scheme, message needs to be encoded in Base64 format. You can specify this message as base64 encoded plain text message e.g. 'Please Wait.' or it can be HTML paragraph or a body string encoded as base64 string E.g. '<p> Please Wait </p>'. Base64 encoded string for this html is 'PHA+IFBsZWFzZSBXYWl0IDwvcD4='

### Nested Schema for `cookie_stickiness`

Optional:

- `add_httponly` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--cookie_stickiness--add_httponly))
- `add_secure` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--cookie_stickiness--add_secure))

- `path` (String) Path. The name of the path for the cookie. If no path is specified here, no path will be set for the cookie

- `samesite_strict` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--cookie_stickiness--samesite_strict))
- `ttl` (Number) TTL. If specified, a cookie with the TTL will be generated if the cookie is not present. If the TTL is present and zero, the generated cookie will be a session cookie. TTL value is in milliseconds

<a id="nestedblock--cors_policy"></a>
### Nested Schema for `cors_policy`

Optional:

- `allow_credentials` (Boolean) Allow Credentials. Specifies whether the resource allows credentials
- `allow_headers` (String) Allow Headers. Specifies the content for the access-control-allow-headers header
- `allow_methods` (String) Allow Methods. Specifies the content for the access-control-allow-methods header
- `allow_origin` (List of String) Allow Origin. Specifies the origins that will be allowed to do CORS requests. An origin is allowed if either allow_origin or allow_origin_regex match
- `allow_origin_regex` (List of String) Allow Origin Regex. Specifies regex patterns that match allowed origins. An origin is allowed if either allow_origin or allow_origin_regex match
- `disabled` (Boolean) Disabled. Disable the CorsPolicy for a particular route. This is useful when virtual-host has CorsPolicy, but we need to disable it on a specific route. The value of this field is ignored for virtual-host
- `expose_headers` (String) Expose Headers. Specifies the content for the access-control-expose-headers header
- `maximum_age` (Number) Maximum Age. Specifies the content for the access-control-max-age header in seconds. This indicates the maximum number of seconds the results can be cached A value of -1 will disable caching. Maximum permitted value is 86400 seconds (24 hours)

### Nested Schema for `ddos_mitigation_rules.ddos_client_source`

Optional:

- `asn_list` (Block, Optional) ASN Match List. An unordered set of RFC 6793 defined 4-byte AS numbers that can be used to create allow or deny lists for use in network policy or service policy. It can be used to create the allow list only for DNS Load Balancer. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--ddos_mitigation_rules--ddos_client_source--asn_list))
- `country_list` (List of String) Country List. Sources that are located in one of the countries in the given list
- `ja4_tls_fingerprint_matcher` (Block, Optional) JA4 TLS Fingerprint Matcher. An extended version of JA3 that includes additional fields for more comprehensive fingerprinting of SSL/TLS clients and potentially has a different structure and length. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--ddos_mitigation_rules--ddos_client_source--ja4_tls_fingerprint_matcher))
- `tls_fingerprint_matcher` (Block, Optional) TLS Fingerprint Matcher. A TLS fingerprint matcher specifies multiple criteria for matching a TLS fingerprint. The set of supported positve match criteria includes a list of known classes of TLS fingerprints and a list of exact values. The match is considered successful if either of these positive criteria are satisfied and the input fingerprint is not one of the excluded values. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--ddos_mitigation_rules--ddos_client_source--tls_fingerprint_matcher))

<a id="nestedblock--ddos_mitigation_rules--ddos_client_source--tls_fingerprint_matcher"></a>
### Nested Schema for `ddos_mitigation_rules.ddos_client_source.tls_fingerprint_matcher`

Optional:

- `classes` (List of String) TLS fingerprint classes. A list of known classes of TLS fingerprints to match the input TLS JA3 fingerprint against.
- `exact_values` (List of String) Exact Values. A list of exact TLS JA3 fingerprints to match the input TLS JA3 fingerprint against.
- `excluded_values` (List of String) Excluded Values. A list of TLS JA3 fingerprints to be excluded when matching the input TLS JA3 fingerprint. This can be used to skip known false positives when using one or more known TLS fingerprint classes in the enclosing matcher.

Different load balancing algorithms supported When a connection to a endpoint in an upstream cluster is required, the load balancer uses loadbalancer_algorithm to determine which host is selected. - ROUND_ROBIN: ROUND_ROBIN Policy in which each healthy/available upstream endpoint is selected in round robin order. - LEAST_REQUEST: LEAST_REQUEST Policy in which loadbalancer picks the upstream endpoint which has the fewest active requests - RING_HASH: RING_HASH Policy im... ### Nested Schema for `default_pool.advanced_options`

Optional:

- `auto_http_config` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--default_pool--advanced_options--auto_http_config))

CircuitBreaker provides a mechanism for watching failures in upstream connections or requests and if the failures reach a certain threshold, automatically fail subsequent requests which allows to apply back pressure on downstream quickly. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--default_pool--advanced_options--circuit_breaker))
- `connection_timeout` (Number) Connection Timeout. The timeout for new network connections to endpoints in the cluster. This is specified in milliseconds. The default value is 2 seconds

- `http2_options` (Block, Optional) Http2 Protocol Options. Http2 Protocol options for upstream connections (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--default_pool--advanced_options--http2_options))
- `http_idle_timeout` (Number) HTTP Idle Timeout. The idle timeout for upstream connection pool connections. The idle timeout is defined as the period in which there are no active requests. When the idle timeout is reached the connection will be closed. Note that request based timeouts mean that HTTP/2 PINGs will not keep the connection alive. This is specified in milliseconds. The default value is 5 minutes.
- `no_panic_threshold` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--default_pool--advanced_options--no_panic_threshold))
- `outlier_detection` (Block, Optional) Outlier Detection. Outlier detection and ejection is the process of dynamically determining whether some number of hosts in an upstream cluster are performing unlike the others and removing them from the healthy load balancing set. Outlier detection is a form of passive health checking. Algorithm 1. A endpoint is determined to be an outlier (based on configured number of consecutive_5xx or consecutive_gateway_failures) . 2. If no endpoints have been ejected, loadbalancer will eject the host i... (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--default_pool--advanced_options--outlier_detection))
- `panic_threshold` (Number) Panic threshold. x-example:'25' Configure a threshold (percentage of unhealthy endpoints) below which all endpoints will be considered for load balancing ignoring its health status.
- `proxy_protocol_v1` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--default_pool--advanced_options--proxy_protocol_v1))
- `proxy_protocol_v2` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--default_pool--advanced_options--proxy_protocol_v2))

<a id="nestedblock--default_pool--advanced_options--circuit_breaker"></a>
### Nested Schema for `default_pool.advanced_options.circuit_breaker`

Optional:

- `connection_limit` (Number) Connection Limit. The maximum number of connections that loadbalancer will establish to all hosts in an upstream cluster. In practice this is only applicable to TCP and HTTP/1.1 clusters since HTTP/2 uses a single connection to each host. Remove endpoint out of load balancing decision, if number of connections reach connection limit.
- `max_requests` (Number) Maximum Request Count. The maximum number of requests that can be outstanding to all hosts in a cluster at any given time. In practice this is applicable to HTTP/2 clusters since HTTP/1.1 clusters are governed by the maximum connections (connection_limit). Remove endpoint out of load balancing decision, if requests exceed this count.
- `pending_requests` (Number) Pending Requests. The maximum number of requests that will be queued while waiting for a ready connection pool connection. Since HTTP/2 requests are sent over a single connection, this circuit breaker only comes into play as the initial connection is created, as requests will be multiplexed immediately afterwards. For HTTP/1.1, requests are added to the list of pending requests whenever there arent enough upstream connections available to immediately dispatch the request, so this circuit b...
- `priority` (String) Routing Priority. Priority routing for each request. Different connection pools are used based on the priority selected for the request. Also, circuit-breaker configuration at destination cluster is chosen based on selected priority. Default routing mechanism High-Priority routing mechanism. Possible values are `DEFAULT`, `HIGH`.
- `retries` (Number) Retry Count. The maximum number of retries that can be outstanding to all hosts in a cluster at any given time. Remove endpoint out of load balancing decision, if retries for request exceed this count.

<a id="nestedblock--default_pool--advanced_options--outlier_detection"></a>
### Nested Schema for `default_pool.advanced_options.outlier_detection`

Optional:

- `base_ejection_time` (Number) Base Ejection Time. The base time that a host is ejected for. The real time is equal to the base time multiplied by the number of times the host has been ejected. This causes hosts to get ejected for longer periods if they continue to fail. Defaults to 30000ms or 30s. Specified in milliseconds.
- `consecutive_5xx` (Number) Consecutive 5xx Count. If an upstream endpoint returns some number of consecutive 5xx, it will be ejected. Note that in this case a 5xx means an actual 5xx respond code, or an event that would cause the HTTP router to return one on the upstreams behalf(reset, connection failure, etc.) consecutive_5xx indicates the number of consecutive 5xx responses required before a consecutive 5xx ejection occurs. Defaults to 5.
- `consecutive_gateway_failure` (Number) Consecutive Gateway Failure. If an upstream endpoint returns some number of consecutive gateway errors (502, 503 or 504 status code), it will be ejected. Note that this includes events that would cause the HTTP router to return one of these status codes on the upstreams behalf (reset, connection failure, etc.). consecutive_gateway_failure indicates the number of consecutive gateway failures before a consecutive gateway failure ejection occurs. Defaults to 5.
- `interval` (Number) Interval. The time interval between ejection analysis sweeps. This can result in both new ejections as well as endpoints being returned to service. Defaults to 10000ms or 10s. Specified in milliseconds.
- `max_ejection_percent` (Number) Max Ejection Percentage. The maximum % of an upstream cluster that can be ejected due to outlier detection. Defaults to 10% but will eject at least one host regardless of the value.


<a id="nestedblock--default_pool--advanced_options--proxy_protocol_v1"></a>
### Nested Schema for `default_pool.advanced_options.proxy_protocol_v1`


<a id="nestedblock--default_pool--advanced_options--proxy_protocol_v2"></a>
### Nested Schema for `default_pool.advanced_options.proxy_protocol_v2`



<a id="nestedblock--default_pool--automatic_port"></a>
### Nested Schema for `default_pool.automatic_port`

- `k8s_service` (Block, Optional) K8s Service Name on given Sites. Specify origin server with K8s service name and site information (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--default_pool--origin_servers--k8s_service))
- `labels` (Block, Optional) Origin Server Labels. Add Labels for this origin server, these labels can be used to form subset. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--default_pool--origin_servers--labels))
- `private_ip` (Block, Optional) IP address on given Sites. Specify origin server with private or public IP address and site information (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--default_pool--origin_servers--private_ip))
- `private_name` (Block, Optional) DNS Name on given Sites. Specify origin server with private or public DNS name and site information (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--default_pool--origin_servers--private_name))
- `public_ip` (Block, Optional) Public IP. Specify origin server with public IP address (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--default_pool--origin_servers--public_ip))
- `public_name` (Block, Optional) Public DNS Name. Specify origin server with public DNS name (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--default_pool--origin_servers--public_name))

Optional:

- `inside_network` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--default_pool--origin_servers--k8s_service--inside_network))
- `outside_network` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--default_pool--origin_servers--k8s_service--outside_network))
- `protocol` (String) Protocol Type. Type of protocol - PROTOCOL_TCP: TCP - PROTOCOL_UDP: UDP. Possible values are `PROTOCOL_TCP`, `PROTOCOL_UDP`.
- `service_name` (String) Service Name. K8s service name of the origin server will be listed, including the namespace and cluster-id. For vK8s services, you need to enter a string with the format servicename.namespace:cluster-id. If the servicename is 'frontend', namespace is 'speedtest' and cluster-id is 'prod', then you will enter 'frontend.speedtest:prod'. Both namespace and cluster-id are optional.
- `site_locator` (Block, Optional) Site or Virtual Site. This message defines a reference to a site or virtual site object (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--default_pool--origin_servers--k8s_service--site_locator))
- `snat_pool` (Block, Optional) Snat Pool. Snat Pool configuration (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--default_pool--origin_servers--k8s_service--snat_pool))
- `vk8s_networks` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--default_pool--origin_servers--k8s_service--vk8s_networks))

<a id="nestedblock--default_pool_list--pools"></a>
### Nested Schema for `default_pool_list.pools`

Optional:

- `cluster` (Block, Optional) Object reference. This type establishes a direct reference from one object(the referrer) to another(the referred). Such a reference is in form of tenant/namespace/name (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--default_pool_list--pools--cluster))
- `endpoint_subsets` (Block, Optional) Origin Servers Subsets. Upstream origin pool may be configured to divide its origin servers into subsets based on metadata attached to the origin servers. Routes may then specify the metadata that a endpoint must match in order to be selected by the load balancer For origin servers which are discovered in K8S or Consul cluster, the label of the service is merged with endpoint's labels. In case of Consul, the label is derived from the 'Tag' field. For labels that are common between configured ... (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--default_pool_list--pools--endpoint_subsets))
- `pool` (Block, Optional) Object reference. This type establishes a direct reference from one object(the referrer) to another(the referred). Such a reference is in form of tenant/namespace/name (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--default_pool_list--pools--pool))
- `priority` (Number) Priority. Priority of this origin pool, valid only with multiple origin pools. Value of 0 will make the pool as lowest priority origin pool Priority of 1 means highest priority and is considered active. When active origin pool is not available, lower priority origin pools are made active as per the increasing priority.
- `weight` (Number) Weight. Weight of this origin pool, valid only with multiple origin pool. Value of 0 will disable the pool

### Nested Schema for `default_route_pools`

Optional:

- `cluster` (Block, Optional) Object reference. This type establishes a direct reference from one object(the referrer) to another(the referred). Such a reference is in form of tenant/namespace/name (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--default_route_pools--cluster))
- `endpoint_subsets` (Block, Optional) Origin Servers Subsets. Upstream origin pool may be configured to divide its origin servers into subsets based on metadata attached to the origin servers. Routes may then specify the metadata that a endpoint must match in order to be selected by the load balancer For origin servers which are discovered in K8S or Consul cluster, the label of the service is merged with endpoint's labels. In case of Consul, the label is derived from the 'Tag' field. For labels that are common between configured ... (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--default_route_pools--endpoint_subsets))
- `pool` (Block, Optional) Object reference. This type establishes a direct reference from one object(the referrer) to another(the referred). Such a reference is in form of tenant/namespace/name (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--default_route_pools--pool))
- `priority` (Number) Priority. Priority of this origin pool, valid only with multiple origin pools. Value of 0 will make the pool as lowest priority origin pool Priority of 1 means highest priority and is considered active. When active origin pool is not available, lower priority origin pools are made active as per the increasing priority.
- `weight` (Number) Weight. Weight of this origin pool, valid only with multiple origin pool. Value of 0 will disable the pool

- `namespace` (String) Namespace. When a configuration object(e.g. virtual_host) refers to another(e.g route) then namespace will hold the referred object's(e.g. route's) namespace.
- `tenant` (String) Tenant. When a configuration object(e.g. virtual_host) refers to another(e.g route) then tenant will hold the referred object's(e.g. route's) tenant.

Optional:

- `captcha_challenge_parameters` (Block, Optional) Captcha Challenge Parameters. Enables loadbalancer to perform captcha challenge Captcha challenge will be based on Google Recaptcha. With this feature enabled, only clients that pass the captcha challenge will be allowed to complete the HTTP request. When loadbalancer is configured to do Captcha Challenge, it will redirect the browser to an HTML page on every new HTTP request. This HTML page will have captcha challenge embedded in it. Client will be allowed to make the request only if the cap... (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--enable_challenge--captcha_challenge_parameters))
- `default_captcha_challenge_parameters` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--enable_challenge--default_captcha_challenge_parameters))
- `default_js_challenge_parameters` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--enable_challenge--default_js_challenge_parameters))
- `default_mitigation_settings` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--enable_challenge--default_mitigation_settings))
- `js_challenge_parameters` (Block, Optional) Javascript Challenge Parameters. Enables loadbalancer to perform client browser compatibility test by redirecting to a page with Javascript. With this feature enabled, only clients that are capable of executing Javascript(mostly browsers) will be allowed to complete the HTTP request. When loadbalancer is configured to do Javascript Challenge, it will redirect the browser to an HTML page on every new HTTP request. This HTML page will have Javascript embedded in it. Loadbalancer chooses a set o... (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--enable_challenge--js_challenge_parameters))
- `malicious_user_mitigation` (Block, Optional) Object reference. This type establishes a direct reference from one object(the referrer) to another(the referred). Such a reference is in form of tenant/namespace/name (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--enable_challenge--malicious_user_mitigation))

<a id="nestedblock--enable_challenge--captcha_challenge_parameters"></a>
### Nested Schema for `enable_challenge.captcha_challenge_parameters`

Optional:

- `cookie_expiry` (Number) Cookie Expiration Period. Cookie expiration period, in seconds. An expired cookie causes the loadbalancer to issue a new challenge.
- `custom_page` (String) Custom message for Captcha Challenge. Custom message is of type uri_ref. Currently supported URL schemes is string:///. For string:/// scheme, message needs to be encoded in Base64 format. You can specify this message as base64 encoded plain text message e.g. 'Please Wait.' or it can be HTML paragraph or a body string encoded as base64 string E.g. '<p> Please Wait </p>'. Base64 encoded string for this html is 'PHA+IFBsZWFzZSBXYWl0IDwvcD4='

Optional:

As a prerequisite, the domain must be delegated to F5 Distributed Cloud using Delegated domain feature or a DNS CNAME record should be created in your DNS provider's portal.

<a id="nestedblock--https"></a>
### Nested Schema for `https`

Optional:

- `add_hsts` (Boolean) Add HSTS Header. Add HTTP Strict-Transport-Security response header
- `append_server_name` (String) Append header value. Define the header value for the header name server. If header value is already present, it is not overwritten and passed as-is.
- `coalescing_options` (Block, Optional) TLS Coalescing Options. TLS connection coalescing configuration (not compatible with mTLS) (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--https--coalescing_options))
- `connection_idle_timeout` (Number) Connection Idle Timeout. The idle timeout for downstream connections. The idle timeout is defined as the period in which there are no active requests. When the idle timeout is reached the connection will be closed. Note that request based timeouts mean that HTTP/2 PINGs will not keep the connection alive. This is specified in milliseconds. The default value is 2 minutes.
- `default_header` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--https--default_header))
- `default_loadbalancer` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--https--default_loadbalancer))
- `disable_path_normalize` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--https--disable_path_normalize))
- `enable_path_normalize` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--https--enable_path_normalize))
- `http_protocol_options` (Block, Optional) HTTP Protocol Configuration Options. HTTP protocol configuration options for downstream connections (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--https--http_protocol_options))
- `http_redirect` (Boolean) HTTP Redirect to HTTPS. Redirect HTTP traffic to HTTPS
- `non_default_loadbalancer` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--https--non_default_loadbalancer))
- `pass_through` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--https--pass_through))
- `port` (Number) HTTPS Port. HTTPS port to Listen.
- `port_ranges` (String) Port Ranges. A string containing a comma separated list of port ranges. Each port range consists of a single port or two ports separated by '-'.
- `server_name` (String) Modify header value. Define the header value for the header name server. This will overwrite existing values, if any, for the server header.
- `tls_cert_params` (Block, Optional) TLS Parameters. Select TLS Parameters and Certificates (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--https--tls_cert_params))
- `tls_parameters` (Block, Optional) Inline TLS Parameters. Inline TLS parameters (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--https--tls_parameters))

<a id="nestedblock--https--tls_cert_params"></a>
### Nested Schema for `https.tls_cert_params`

Optional:

- `certificates` (Block List) Certificates. Select one or more certificates with any domain names. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--https--tls_cert_params--certificates))

- `tls_config` (Block, Optional) TLS Config. This defines various options to configure TLS configuration parameters (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--https--tls_cert_params--tls_config))
- `use_mtls` (Block, Optional) Clients TLS validation context. Validation context for downstream client TLS connections (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--https--tls_cert_params--use_mtls))

<a id="nestedblock--https--tls_cert_params--certificates"></a>
### Nested Schema for `https.tls_cert_params.certificates`

Optional:

- `name` (String) Name. When a configuration object(e.g. virtual_host) refers to another(e.g route) then name will hold the referred object's(e.g. route's) name.
- `namespace` (String) Namespace. When a configuration object(e.g. virtual_host) refers to another(e.g route) then namespace will hold the referred object's(e.g. route's) namespace.
- `tenant` (String) Tenant. When a configuration object(e.g. virtual_host) refers to another(e.g route) then tenant will hold the referred object's(e.g. route's) tenant.

<a id="nestedblock--https--tls_cert_params--use_mtls"></a>
### Nested Schema for `https.tls_cert_params.use_mtls`

Optional:

- `client_certificate_optional` (Boolean) Client Certificate Optional. Client certificate is optional. If the client has provided a certificate, the load balancer will verify it. If certification verification fails, the connection will be terminated. If the client does not provide a certificate, the connection will be accepted.
- `crl` (Block, Optional) Object reference. This type establishes a direct reference from one object(the referrer) to another(the referred). Such a reference is in form of tenant/namespace/name (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--https--tls_cert_params--use_mtls--crl))
- `no_crl` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--https--tls_cert_params--use_mtls--no_crl))
- `trusted_ca` (Block, Optional) Object reference. This type establishes a direct reference from one object(the referrer) to another(the referred). Such a reference is in form of tenant/namespace/name (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--https--tls_cert_params--use_mtls--trusted_ca))
- `trusted_ca_url` (String) Inline Root CA Certificate (legacy). Upload a Root CA Certificate specifically for this Load Balancer
- `xfcc_disabled` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--https--tls_cert_params--use_mtls--xfcc_disabled))
- `xfcc_options` (Block, Optional) XFCC Header Elements. X-Forwarded-Client-Cert header elements to be added to requests (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--https--tls_cert_params--use_mtls--xfcc_options))

<a id="nestedblock--https_auto_cert"></a>
### Nested Schema for `https_auto_cert`

Optional:

- `add_hsts` (Boolean) Add HSTS Header. Add HTTP Strict-Transport-Security response header
- `append_server_name` (String) Append header value. Define the header value for the header name server. If header value is already present, it is not overwritten and passed as-is.
- `coalescing_options` (Block, Optional) TLS Coalescing Options. TLS connection coalescing configuration (not compatible with mTLS) (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--https_auto_cert--coalescing_options))
- `connection_idle_timeout` (Number) Connection Idle Timeout. The idle timeout for downstream connections. The idle timeout is defined as the period in which there are no active requests. When the idle timeout is reached the connection will be closed. Note that request based timeouts mean that HTTP/2 PINGs will not keep the connection alive. This is specified in milliseconds. The default value is 2 minutes.
- `default_header` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--https_auto_cert--default_header))
- `default_loadbalancer` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--https_auto_cert--default_loadbalancer))
- `disable_path_normalize` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--https_auto_cert--disable_path_normalize))
- `enable_path_normalize` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--https_auto_cert--enable_path_normalize))
- `http_protocol_options` (Block, Optional) HTTP Protocol Configuration Options. HTTP protocol configuration options for downstream connections (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--https_auto_cert--http_protocol_options))
- `http_redirect` (Boolean) HTTP Redirect to HTTPS. Redirect HTTP traffic to HTTPS
- `no_mtls` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--https_auto_cert--no_mtls))
- `non_default_loadbalancer` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--https_auto_cert--non_default_loadbalancer))
- `pass_through` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--https_auto_cert--pass_through))
- `port` (Number) HTTPS Listen Port. HTTPS port to Listen.
- `port_ranges` (String) Port Ranges. A string containing a comma separated list of port ranges. Each port range consists of a single port or two ports separated by '-'.
- `server_name` (String) Modify header value. Define the header value for the header name server. This will overwrite existing values, if any, for the server header.
- `tls_config` (Block, Optional) TLS Config. This defines various options to configure TLS configuration parameters (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--https_auto_cert--tls_config))
- `use_mtls` (Block, Optional) Clients TLS validation context. Validation context for downstream client TLS connections (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--https_auto_cert--use_mtls))

### Nested Schema for `https_auto_cert.tls_config.custom_security`

Optional:

- `cipher_suites` (List of String) Cipher Suites. The TLS listener will only support the specified cipher list.
- `max_version` (String) TLS Protocol. TlsProtocol is enumeration of supported TLS versions F5 Distributed Cloud will choose the optimal TLS version. Possible values are `TLS_AUTO`, `TLSv1_0`, `TLSv1_1`, `TLSv1_2`, `TLSv1_3`.
- `min_version` (String) TLS Protocol. TlsProtocol is enumeration of supported TLS versions F5 Distributed Cloud will choose the optimal TLS version. Possible values are `TLS_AUTO`, `TLSv1_0`, `TLSv1_1`, `TLSv1_2`, `TLSv1_3`.

<a id="nestedblock--js_challenge"></a>
### Nested Schema for `js_challenge`

Optional:

- `cookie_expiry` (Number) Cookie Expiration Period. Cookie expiration period, in seconds. An expired cookie causes the loadbalancer to issue a new challenge.
- `custom_page` (String) Custom Message for Javascript Challenge. Custom message is of type uri_ref. Currently supported URL schemes is string:///. For string:/// scheme, message needs to be encoded in Base64 format. You can specify this message as base64 encoded plain text message e.g. 'Please Wait.' or it can be HTML paragraph or a body string encoded as base64 string E.g. '<p> Please Wait </p>'. Base64 encoded string for this html is 'PHA+IFBsZWFzZSBXYWl0IDwvcD4='
- `js_script_delay` (Number) Javascript Delay. Delay introduced by Javascript, in milliseconds.


<a id="nestedblock--jwt_validation"></a>
### Nested Schema for `jwt_validation`

Optional:

- `action` (Block, Optional) Action. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--jwt_validation--action))
- `jwks_config` (Block, Optional) JSON Web Key Set (JWKS). The JSON Web Key Set (JWKS) is a set of keys used to verify JSON Web Token (JWT) issued by the Authorization Server. See RFC 7517 for more details. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--jwt_validation--jwks_config))
- `mandatory_claims` (Block, Optional) Mandatory Claims. Configurable Validation of mandatory Claims. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--jwt_validation--mandatory_claims))
- `reserved_claims` (Block, Optional) Reserved claims configuration. Configurable Validation of reserved Claims (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--jwt_validation--reserved_claims))
- `target` (Block, Optional) Target. Define endpoints for which JWT token validation will be performed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--jwt_validation--target))
- `token_location` (Block, Optional) Token Location. Location of JWT in Http request (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--jwt_validation--token_location))

<a id="nestedblock--jwt_validation--jwks_config"></a>
### Nested Schema for `jwt_validation.jwks_config`

Optional:

- `cleartext` (String) JSON Web Key Set (JWKS). The JSON Web Key Set (JWKS) is a set of keys used to verify JSON Web Token (JWT) issued by the Authorization Server. See RFC 7517 for more details.


<a id="nestedblock--jwt_validation--mandatory_claims"></a>

<a id="nestedblock--l7_ddos_action_js_challenge"></a>
### Nested Schema for `l7_ddos_action_js_challenge`

Optional:

- `cookie_expiry` (Number) Cookie Expiration Period. Cookie expiration period, in seconds. An expired cookie causes the loadbalancer to issue a new challenge.
- `custom_page` (String) Custom Message for Javascript Challenge. Custom message is of type uri_ref. Currently supported URL schemes is string:///. For string:/// scheme, message needs to be encoded in Base64 format. You can specify this message as base64 encoded plain text message e.g. 'Please Wait.' or it can be HTML paragraph or a body string encoded as base64 string E.g. '<p> Please Wait </p>'. Base64 encoded string for this html is 'PHA+IFBsZWFzZSBXYWl0IDwvcD4='
- `js_script_delay` (Number) Javascript Delay. Delay introduced by Javascript, in milliseconds.

Optional:

- `clientside_action_captcha_challenge` (Block, Optional) Captcha Challenge Parameters. Enables loadbalancer to perform captcha challenge Captcha challenge will be based on Google Recaptcha. With this feature enabled, only clients that pass the captcha challenge will be allowed to complete the HTTP request. When loadbalancer is configured to do Captcha Challenge, it will redirect the browser to an HTML page on every new HTTP request. This HTML page will have captcha challenge embedded in it. Client will be allowed to make the request only if the cap... (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--l7_ddos_protection--clientside_action_captcha_challenge))

When loadbalancer is configured to do Javascript Challenge, it will redirect the browser to an HTML page on every new HTTP request. This HTML page will have Javascript embedded in it. Loadbalancer chooses a set o... (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--l7_ddos_protection--clientside_action_js_challenge))

- `ddos_policy_custom` (Block, Optional) Object reference. This type establishes a direct reference from one object(the referrer) to another(the referred). Such a reference is in form of tenant/namespace/name (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--l7_ddos_protection--ddos_policy_custom))
- `ddos_policy_none` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--l7_ddos_protection--ddos_policy_none))
