<a id="nestedblock--more_option"></a>
### Nested Schema for `more_option`

Optional:

- `buffer_policy` (Block, Optional) Buffer Configuration. Some upstream applications are not capable of handling streamed data. This config enables buffering the entire request before sending to upstream application. We can specify the maximum buffer size and buffer interval with this config. Buffering can be enabled and disabled at VirtualHost and Route levels Route level buffer configuration takes precedence. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--more_option--buffer_policy))
- `compression_params` (Block, Optional) Compression Parameters. Enables loadbalancer to compress dispatched data from an upstream service upon client request. The content is compressed and then sent to the client with the appropriate headers if either response and request allow. Only GZIP compression is supported. By default compression will be skipped when: A request does NOT contain accept-encoding header. A request includes accept-encoding header, but it does not contain gzip or *. A request includes accept-encoding ... (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--more_option--compression_params))
- `custom_errors` (Block, Optional) Custom Error Responses. Map of integer error codes as keys and string values that can be used to provide custom http pages for each error code. Key of the map can be either response code class or HTTP Error code. Response code classes for key is configured as follows 3 -- for 3xx response code class 4 -- for 4xx response code class 5 -- for 5xx response code class Value of the map is string which represents custom HTTP responses. Specific response code takes preference when both response code... (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--more_option--custom_errors))
- `disable_default_error_pages` (Boolean) Disable Default Error Pages. Disable the use of default F5XC error pages.
- `disable_path_normalize` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--more_option--disable_path_normalize))
- `enable_path_normalize` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--more_option--enable_path_normalize))
- `idle_timeout` (Number) Idle Timeout. The amount of time that a stream can exist without upstream or downstream activity, in milliseconds. The stream is terminated with a HTTP 504 (Gateway Timeout) error code if no upstream response header has been received, otherwise the stream is reset.
- `max_request_header_size` (Number) Maximum Request Header Size. The maximum request header size for downstream connections, in KiB. A HTTP 431 (Request Header Fields Too Large) error code is sent for requests that exceed this size. If multiple load balancers share the same advertise_policy, the highest value configured across all such load balancers is used for all the load balancers in question.
- `request_cookies_to_add` (Block List) Add Cookies in Cookie Header. Cookies are key-value pairs to be added to HTTP request being routed towards upstream. Cookies specified at this level are applied after cookies from matched Route are applied (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--more_option--request_cookies_to_add))
- `request_cookies_to_remove` (List of String) Remove Cookies from Cookie Header. List of keys of Cookies to be removed from the HTTP request being sent towards upstream.
- `request_headers_to_add` (Block List) Add Request Headers. Headers are key-value pairs to be added to HTTP request being routed towards upstream. Headers specified at this level are applied after headers from matched Route are applied (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--more_option--request_headers_to_add))
- `request_headers_to_remove` (List of String) Remove Request Headers. List of keys of Headers to be removed from the HTTP request being sent towards upstream.
- `response_cookies_to_add` (Block List) Add Set-Cookie Headers. Cookies are name-value pairs along with optional attribute parameters to be added to HTTP response being sent towards downstream. Cookies specified at this level are applied after cookies from matched Route are applied (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--more_option--response_cookies_to_add))
- `response_cookies_to_remove` (List of String) Remove Cookies from Set-Cookie Headers. List of name of Cookies to be removed from the HTTP response being sent towards downstream. Entire set-cookie header will be removed
- `response_headers_to_add` (Block List) Add Response Headers. Headers are key-value pairs to be added to HTTP response being sent towards downstream. Headers specified at this level are applied after headers from matched Route are applied (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--more_option--response_headers_to_add))
- `response_headers_to_remove` (List of String) Remove Response Headers. List of keys of Headers to be removed from the HTTP response being sent towards downstream.

<a id="nestedblock--more_option--buffer_policy"></a>
### Nested Schema for `more_option.buffer_policy`

Optional:

- `disabled` (Boolean) Disable. Disable buffering for a particular route. This is useful when virtual-host has buffering, but we need to disable it on a specific route. The value of this field is ignored for virtual-host
- `max_request_bytes` (Number) Max Request Bytes. The maximum request size that the filter will buffer before the connection manager will stop buffering and return a RequestEntityTooLarge (413) response.


<a id="nestedblock--more_option--compression_params"></a>
### Nested Schema for `more_option.compression_params`

Optional:

- `content_length` (Number) Content Length. Minimum response length, in bytes, which will trigger compression. The default value is 30.
- `content_type` (List of String) Content Type. Set of strings that allows specifying which mime-types yield compression When this field is not defined, compression will be applied to the following mime-types: 'application/javascript' 'application/json', 'application/xhtml+xml' 'image/svg+xml' 'text/css' 'text/html' 'text/plain' 'text/xml'
- `disable_on_etag_header` (Boolean) Disable On Etag Header. If true, disables compression when the response contains an etag header. When it is false, weak etags will be preserved and the ones that require strong validation will be removed.
- `remove_accept_encoding_header` (Boolean) Remove Accept-Encoding Header. If true, removes accept-encoding from the request headers before dispatching it to the upstream so that responses do not get compressed before reaching the filter.

- `overwrite` (Boolean) Overwrite. Should the value be overwritten? If true, the value is overwritten to existing values. Default value is do not overwrite

<a id="nestedblock--more_option--response_cookies_to_add"></a>
### Nested Schema for `more_option.response_cookies_to_add`

Optional:

- `add_domain` (String) Add Domain. Add domain attribute
- `add_expiry` (String) Add expiry. Add expiry attribute
- `add_httponly` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--more_option--response_cookies_to_add--add_httponly))

- `ignore_expiry` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--more_option--response_cookies_to_add--ignore_expiry))
- `ignore_httponly` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--more_option--response_cookies_to_add--ignore_httponly))
- `ignore_max_age` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--more_option--response_cookies_to_add--ignore_max_age))
- `ignore_partitioned` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--more_option--response_cookies_to_add--ignore_partitioned))
- `ignore_path` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--more_option--response_cookies_to_add--ignore_path))
- `ignore_samesite` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--more_option--response_cookies_to_add--ignore_samesite))
- `ignore_secure` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--more_option--response_cookies_to_add--ignore_secure))
- `ignore_value` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--more_option--response_cookies_to_add--ignore_value))
- `max_age_value` (Number) Add Max Age. Add max age attribute
- `name` (String) Name. Name of the cookie in Cookie header.
- `overwrite` (Boolean) Overwrite. Should the value be overwritten? If true, the value is overwritten to existing values. Default value is do not overwrite
- `samesite_lax` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--more_option--response_cookies_to_add--samesite_lax))
- `samesite_none` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--more_option--response_cookies_to_add--samesite_none))
- `samesite_strict` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--more_option--response_cookies_to_add--samesite_strict))
- `secret_value` (Block, Optional) Secret. SecretType is used in an object to indicate a sensitive/confidential field (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--more_option--response_cookies_to_add--secret_value))
- `value` (String) Value. Value of the Cookie header.

### Nested Schema for `origin_server_subset_rule_list`

Optional:

- `origin_server_subset_rules` (Block List) Origin Server Subset Rules. Origin Server Subset Rules allow users to define match condition on Client (IP address, ASN, Country), IP Reputation, Regional Edge names, Request for subset selection of origin servers. Origin Server Subset is a sequential engine where rules are evaluated one after the other. It's important to define the correct order for Origin Server Subset to get the intended result, rules are evaluated from top to bottom in the list. When an Origin server subset rule is matche... (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--origin_server_subset_rule_list--origin_server_subset_rules))

<a id="nestedblock--origin_server_subset_rule_list--origin_server_subset_rules"></a>
### Nested Schema for `origin_server_subset_rule_list.origin_server_subset_rules`

Optional:

- `any_asn` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--origin_server_subset_rule_list--origin_server_subset_rules--any_asn))
- `any_ip` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--origin_server_subset_rule_list--origin_server_subset_rules--any_ip))
- `asn_list` (Block, Optional) ASN Match List. An unordered set of RFC 6793 defined 4-byte AS numbers that can be used to create allow or deny lists for use in network policy or service policy. It can be used to create the allow list only for DNS Load Balancer. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--origin_server_subset_rule_list--origin_server_subset_rules--asn_list))
- `asn_matcher` (Block, Optional) ASN Matcher. Match any AS number contained in the list of bgp_asn_sets. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--origin_server_subset_rule_list--origin_server_subset_rules--asn_matcher))
- `client_selector` (Block, Optional) Label Selector. This type can be used to establish a 'selector reference' from one object(called selector) to a set of other objects(called selectees) based on the value of expresssions. A label selector is a label query over a set of resources. An empty label selector matches all objects. A null label selector matches no objects. Label selector is immutable. expressions is a list of strings of label selection expression. Each string has ',' separated values which are 'AND' and all strings ar... (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--origin_server_subset_rule_list--origin_server_subset_rules--client_selector))
- `country_codes` (List of String) Country Codes List. List of Country Codes
- `ip_matcher` (Block, Optional) IP Prefix Matcher. Match any ip prefix contained in the list of ip_prefix_sets. The result of the match is inverted if invert_matcher is true. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--origin_server_subset_rule_list--origin_server_subset_rules--ip_matcher))
- `ip_prefix_list` (Block, Optional) IP Prefix Match List. List of IP Prefix strings to match against. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--origin_server_subset_rule_list--origin_server_subset_rules--ip_prefix_list))
- `metadata` (Block, Optional) Message Metadata. MessageMetaType is metadata (common attributes) of a message that only certain messages have. This information is propagated to the metadata of a child object that gets created from the containing message during view processing. The information in this type can be specified by user during create and replace APIs. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--origin_server_subset_rule_list--origin_server_subset_rules--metadata))
- `none` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--origin_server_subset_rule_list--origin_server_subset_rules--none))
- `origin_server_subsets_action` (Block, Optional) Action. Add labels to select one or more origin servers. Note: The pre-requisite settings to be configured in the origin pool are: 1. Add labels to origin servers 2. Enable subset load balancing in the Origin Server Subsets section and configure keys in origin server subsets classes (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--origin_server_subset_rule_list--origin_server_subset_rules--origin_server_subsets_action))
- `re_name_list` (List of String) RE Names. List of RE names for match

With this feature enabled, only clients that pass the captcha challenge will be allowed to complete the HTTP request. When loadbalancer is configured to do Captcha Challenge, it will redirect the browser to an HTML page on every new HTTP request. This HTML page will have captcha challenge embedded in it. Client will be allowed to make the request only if the cap... (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--policy_based_challenge--captcha_challenge_parameters))

- `js_challenge_parameters` (Block, Optional) Javascript Challenge Parameters. Enables loadbalancer to perform client browser compatibility test by redirecting to a page with Javascript. With this feature enabled, only clients that are capable of executing Javascript(mostly browsers) will be allowed to complete the HTTP request. When loadbalancer is configured to do Javascript Challenge, it will redirect the browser to an HTML page on every new HTTP request. This HTML page will have Javascript embedded in it. Loadbalancer chooses a set o... (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--policy_based_challenge--js_challenge_parameters))

- `no_challenge` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--policy_based_challenge--no_challenge))
- `rule_list` (Block, Optional) Challenge Rule List. List of challenge rules to be used in policy based challenge (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--policy_based_challenge--rule_list))
- `temporary_user_blocking` (Block, Optional) Temporary User Blocking. Specifies configuration for temporary user blocking resulting from user behavior analysis. When Malicious User Mitigation is enabled from service policy rules, users' accessing the application will be analyzed for malicious activity and the configured mitigation actions will be taken on identified malicious users. These mitigation actions include setting up temporary blocking on that user. This configuration specifies settings on how that blocking should be done by th... (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--policy_based_challenge--temporary_user_blocking))

### Nested Schema for `policy_based_challenge.captcha_challenge_parameters`

Optional:

- `cookie_expiry` (Number) Cookie Expiration Period. Cookie expiration period, in seconds. An expired cookie causes the loadbalancer to issue a new challenge.
- `custom_page` (String) Custom message for Captcha Challenge. Custom message is of type uri_ref. Currently supported URL schemes is string:///. For string:/// scheme, message needs to be encoded in Base64 format. You can specify this message as base64 encoded plain text message e.g. 'Please Wait.' or it can be HTML paragraph or a body string encoded as base64 string E.g. '<p> Please Wait </p>'. Base64 encoded string for this html is 'PHA+IFBsZWFzZSBXYWl0IDwvcD4='

A request API is considered to match the rule if all predicates in the rule evaluate to true for that request. Any predicates that are not specified in a rule are implicitly considered to be true. If a request API matches a challenge rule, the configured challenge is enfor... (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--policy_based_challenge--rule_list--rules--spec))

<a id="nestedblock--rate_limit"></a>
### Nested Schema for `rate_limit`

Optional:

- `custom_ip_allowed_list` (Block, Optional) Custom IP Allowed List. IP Allowed list using existing ip_prefix_set objects (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--rate_limit--custom_ip_allowed_list))
- `ip_allowed_list` (Block, Optional) IPv4 Prefix List. x-example: '192.168.20.0/24' List of IPv4 prefixes that represent an endpoint (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--rate_limit--ip_allowed_list))
- `no_ip_allowed_list` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--rate_limit--no_ip_allowed_list))
- `no_policies` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--rate_limit--no_policies))
- `policies` (Block, Optional) Rate Limiter Policy List. List of rate limiter policies to be applied. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--rate_limit--policies))
- `rate_limiter` (Block, Optional) Rate Limit Value. A tuple consisting of a rate limit period unit and the total number of allowed requests for that period. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--rate_limit--rate_limiter))

<a id="nestedblock--rate_limit--custom_ip_allowed_list"></a>
### Nested Schema for `rate_limit.custom_ip_allowed_list`

Optional:

- `rate_limiter_allowed_prefixes` (Block List) List of IP Prefix Sets. References to ip_prefix_set objects. Requests from source IP addresses that are covered by one of the allowed IP Prefixes are not subjected to rate limiting. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--rate_limit--custom_ip_allowed_list--rate_limiter_allowed_prefixes))

<a id="nestedblock--rate_limit--custom_ip_allowed_list--rate_limiter_allowed_prefixes"></a>
### Nested Schema for `rate_limit.custom_ip_allowed_list.rate_limiter_allowed_prefixes`

Optional:

- `name` (String) Name. When a configuration object(e.g. virtual_host) refers to another(e.g route) then name will hold the referred object's(e.g. route's) name.
- `namespace` (String) Namespace. When a configuration object(e.g. virtual_host) refers to another(e.g route) then namespace will hold the referred object's(e.g. route's) namespace.
- `tenant` (String) Tenant. When a configuration object(e.g. virtual_host) refers to another(e.g route) then tenant will hold the referred object's(e.g. route's) tenant.



<a id="nestedblock--rate_limit--ip_allowed_list"></a>
### Nested Schema for `rate_limit.ip_allowed_list`

Optional:

- `prefixes` (List of String) IPv4 Prefix List. List of IPv4 prefixes that represent an endpoint

### Nested Schema for `rate_limit.policies`

<a id="nestedblock--rate_limit--policies--policies"></a>
### Nested Schema for `rate_limit.policies.policies`

Optional:

- `name` (String) Name. When a configuration object(e.g. virtual_host) refers to another(e.g route) then name will hold the referred object's(e.g. route's) name.
- `namespace` (String) Namespace. When a configuration object(e.g. virtual_host) refers to another(e.g route) then namespace will hold the referred object's(e.g. route's) namespace.
- `tenant` (String) Tenant. When a configuration object(e.g. virtual_host) refers to another(e.g route) then tenant will hold the referred object's(e.g. route's) tenant.



<a id="nestedblock--rate_limit--rate_limiter"></a>
### Nested Schema for `rate_limit.rate_limiter`

Optional:

- `action_block` (Block, Optional) Rate Limit Block Action. Action where a user is blocked from making further requests after exceeding rate limit threshold. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--rate_limit--rate_limiter--action_block))
- `burst_multiplier` (Number) Burst Multiplier. The maximum burst of requests to accommodate, expressed as a multiple of the rate.
- `disabled` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--rate_limit--rate_limiter--disabled))
- `leaky_bucket` (Block, Optional) Leaky Bucket Rate Limiter. Leaky-Bucket is the default rate limiter algorithm for F5 (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--rate_limit--rate_limiter--leaky_bucket))
- `period_multiplier` (Number) Periods. This setting, combined with Per Period units, provides a duration
- `token_bucket` (Block, Optional) Token Bucket Rate Limiter. Token-Bucket is a rate limiter algorithm that is stricter with enforcing limits (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--rate_limit--rate_limiter--token_bucket))
- `total_number` (Number) Number Of Requests. The total number of allowed requests per rate-limiting period.
- `unit` (String) Rate Limit Period Unit. Unit for the period per which the rate limit is applied. - SECOND: Second Rate limit period unit is seconds - MINUTE: Minute Rate limit period unit is minutes - HOUR: Hour Rate limit period unit is hours - DAY: Day Rate limit period unit is days. Possible values are `SECOND`, `MINUTE`, `HOUR`.

<a id="nestedblock--rate_limit--rate_limiter--action_block"></a>
### Nested Schema for `rate_limit.rate_limiter.action_block`

Optional:

- `hours` (Block, Optional) Hours. Input Duration Hours (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--rate_limit--rate_limiter--action_block--hours))
- `minutes` (Block, Optional) Minutes. Input Duration Minutes (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--rate_limit--rate_limiter--action_block--minutes))
- `seconds` (Block, Optional) Seconds. Input Duration Seconds (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--rate_limit--rate_limiter--action_block--seconds))

### Nested Schema for `rate_limit.rate_limiter.action_block.seconds`

<a id="nestedblock--ring_hash"></a>
### Nested Schema for `ring_hash`

Optional:

- `hash_policy` (Block List) Hash Policy. Specifies a list of hash policies to use for ring hash load balancing. Each hash policy is evaluated individually and the combined result is used to route the request (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--ring_hash--hash_policy))

<a id="nestedblock--ring_hash--hash_policy"></a>
### Nested Schema for `ring_hash.hash_policy`

Optional:

- `cookie` (Block, Optional) Hashing using Cookie. Two types of cookie affinity: 1. Passive. Takes a cookie that's present in the cookies header and hashes on its value. 2. Generated. Generates and sets a cookie with an expiration (TTL) on the first request from the client in its response to the client, based on the endpoint the request gets sent to. The client then presents this on the next and all subsequent requests. The hash of this is sufficient to ensure these requests get sent to the same endpoint. The cookie is g... (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--ring_hash--hash_policy--cookie))
- `header_name` (String) Header Name. The name or key of the request header that will be used to obtain the hash key
- `source_ip` (Boolean) Source IP. Hash based on source IP address
- `terminal` (Boolean) Terminal. Specify if its a terminal policy

<a id="nestedblock--ring_hash--hash_policy--cookie"></a>
### Nested Schema for `ring_hash.hash_policy.cookie`

Optional:

- `add_httponly` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--ring_hash--hash_policy--cookie--add_httponly))
- `add_secure` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--ring_hash--hash_policy--cookie--add_secure))
- `ignore_httponly` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--ring_hash--hash_policy--cookie--ignore_httponly))
- `ignore_samesite` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--ring_hash--hash_policy--cookie--ignore_samesite))
- `ignore_secure` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--ring_hash--hash_policy--cookie--ignore_secure))
- `name` (String) Name. The name of the cookie that will be used to obtain the hash key. If the cookie is not present and TTL below is not set, no hash will be produced
- `path` (String) Path. The name of the path for the cookie. If no path is specified here, no path will be set for the cookie
- `samesite_lax` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--ring_hash--hash_policy--cookie--samesite_lax))
- `samesite_none` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--ring_hash--hash_policy--cookie--samesite_none))
- `samesite_strict` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--ring_hash--hash_policy--cookie--samesite_strict))
- `ttl` (Number) TTL. If specified, a cookie with the TTL will be generated if the cookie is not present. If the TTL is present and zero, the generated cookie will be a session cookie. TTL value is in milliseconds

<a id="nestedblock--ring_hash--hash_policy--cookie--add_httponly"></a>

<a id="nestedblock--routes"></a>
### Nested Schema for `routes`

Optional:

- `custom_route_object` (Block, Optional) Custom Route Object. A custom route uses a route object created outside of this view. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--custom_route_object))
- `direct_response_route` (Block, Optional) Direct Response Route. A direct response route matches on path, incoming header, incoming port and/or HTTP method and responds directly to the matching traffic (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--direct_response_route))
- `redirect_route` (Block, Optional) Redirect Route. A redirect route matches on path, incoming header, incoming port and/or HTTP method and redirects the matching traffic to a different URL (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--redirect_route))
- `simple_route` (Block, Optional) Simple Route. A simple route matches on path, incoming header, incoming port and/or HTTP method and forwards the matching traffic to the associated pools (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--simple_route))

<a id="nestedblock--routes--custom_route_object"></a>
### Nested Schema for `routes.custom_route_object`

Optional:

- `route_ref` (Block, Optional) Object reference. This type establishes a direct reference from one object(the referrer) to another(the referred). Such a reference is in form of tenant/namespace/name (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--custom_route_object--route_ref))

<a id="nestedblock--routes--custom_route_object--route_ref"></a>
### Nested Schema for `routes.custom_route_object.route_ref`

Optional:

- `name` (String) Name. When a configuration object(e.g. virtual_host) refers to another(e.g route) then name will hold the referred object's(e.g. route's) name.
- `namespace` (String) Namespace. When a configuration object(e.g. virtual_host) refers to another(e.g route) then namespace will hold the referred object's(e.g. route's) namespace.
- `tenant` (String) Tenant. When a configuration object(e.g. virtual_host) refers to another(e.g route) then tenant will hold the referred object's(e.g. route's) tenant.



<a id="nestedblock--routes--direct_response_route"></a>
### Nested Schema for `routes.direct_response_route`

Optional:

- `headers` (Block List) Headers. List of (key, value) headers (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--direct_response_route--headers))
- `http_method` (String) HTTP Method. Specifies the HTTP method used to access a resource. Any HTTP Method. Possible values include `ANY`, `GET`, `HEAD`, `POST`, `PUT`, `DELETE`, `CONNECT`, `OPTIONS`, `TRACE`, `PATCH`, and others.
- `incoming_port` (Block, Optional) Port to Match. Port match of the request can be a range or a specific port (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--direct_response_route--incoming_port))
- `path` (Block, Optional) Path to Match. Path match of the URI can be either be, Prefix match or exact match or regular expression match (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--direct_response_route--path))
- `route_direct_response` (Block, Optional) Direct Response. Send this direct response in case of route match action is direct response (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--direct_response_route--route_direct_response))

<a id="nestedblock--routes--direct_response_route--headers"></a>
### Nested Schema for `routes.direct_response_route.headers`

Optional:

- `exact` (String) Exact. Header value to match exactly
- `invert_match` (Boolean) NOT of match. Invert the result of the match to detect missing header or non-matching value
- `name` (String) Name. Name of the header
- `presence` (Boolean) Presence. If true, check for presence of header
- `regex` (String) Regex. Regex match of the header value in re2 format


<a id="nestedblock--routes--direct_response_route--incoming_port"></a>
### Nested Schema for `routes.direct_response_route.incoming_port`

Optional:

- `no_port_match` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--direct_response_route--incoming_port--no_port_match))
- `port` (Number) Port. Exact Port to match
- `port_ranges` (String) Port range. Port range to match

<a id="nestedblock--routes--direct_response_route--incoming_port--no_port_match"></a>
### Nested Schema for `routes.direct_response_route.incoming_port.no_port_match`



<a id="nestedblock--routes--direct_response_route--path"></a>
### Nested Schema for `routes.direct_response_route.path`

Optional:

- `path` (String) Exact. Exact path value to match
- `prefix` (String) Prefix. Path prefix to match (e.g. the value / will match on all paths)
- `regex` (String) Regex. Regular expression of path match (e.g. the value .* will match on all paths)


<a id="nestedblock--routes--direct_response_route--route_direct_response"></a>
### Nested Schema for `routes.direct_response_route.route_direct_response`

Optional:

- `response_body_encoded` (String) Response Body. Response body to send. Currently supported URL schemes is string:/// for which message should be encoded in Base64 format. The message can be either plain text or html. E.g. '<p> Access Denied </p>'. Base64 encoded string url for this is string:///PHA+IEFjY2VzcyBEZW5pZWQgPC9wPg==
- `response_code` (Number) Response Code. response code to send



<a id="nestedblock--routes--redirect_route"></a>

Optional:

- `headers` (Block List) Headers. List of (key, value) headers (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--redirect_route--headers))
- `http_method` (String) HTTP Method. Specifies the HTTP method used to access a resource. Any HTTP Method. Possible values include `ANY`, `GET`, `HEAD`, `POST`, `PUT`, `DELETE`, `CONNECT`, `OPTIONS`, `TRACE`, `PATCH`, and others.
- `incoming_port` (Block, Optional) Port to Match. Port match of the request can be a range or a specific port (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--redirect_route--incoming_port))
- `path` (Block, Optional) Path to Match. Path match of the URI can be either be, Prefix match or exact match or regular expression match (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--redirect_route--path))
- `route_redirect` (Block, Optional) Redirect. route redirect parameters when match action is redirect. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--redirect_route--route_redirect))

<a id="nestedblock--routes--redirect_route--headers"></a>

- `invert_match` (Boolean) NOT of match. Invert the result of the match to detect missing header or non-matching value
- `name` (String) Name. Name of the header
- `presence` (Boolean) Presence. If true, check for presence of header
- `regex` (String) Regex. Regex match of the header value in re2 format

- `port_ranges` (String) Port range. Port range to match

Optional:

- `path` (String) Exact. Exact path value to match
- `prefix` (String) Prefix. Path prefix to match (e.g. the value / will match on all paths)
- `regex` (String) Regex. Regular expression of path match (e.g. the value .* will match on all paths)


<a id="nestedblock--routes--redirect_route--route_redirect"></a>
### Nested Schema for `routes.redirect_route.route_redirect`

Optional:

- `host_redirect` (String) Host. swap host part of incoming URL in redirect URL
- `path_redirect` (String) Path. swap path part of incoming URL in redirect URL
- `prefix_rewrite` (String) Prefix Rewrite. In Redirect response, the matched prefix (or path) should be swapped with this value. This option allows redirect URLs be dynamically created based on the request
- `proto_redirect` (String) Protocol. swap protocol part of incoming URL in redirect URL The protocol can be swapped with either http or https When incoming-proto option is specified, swapping of protocol is not done.
- `remove_all_params` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--redirect_route--route_redirect--remove_all_params))
- `replace_params` (String) Replace All Parameters.
- `response_code` (Number) Response Code. The HTTP status code to use in the redirect response.
- `retain_all_params` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--redirect_route--route_redirect--retain_all_params))

<a id="nestedblock--routes--redirect_route--route_redirect--remove_all_params"></a>

<a id="nestedblock--routes--simple_route"></a>
### Nested Schema for `routes.simple_route`

Optional:

- `advanced_options` (Block, Optional) Advanced Route Options. Configure advanced options for route like path rewrite, hash policy, etc. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--simple_route--advanced_options))
- `auto_host_rewrite` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--simple_route--auto_host_rewrite))
- `disable_host_rewrite` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--simple_route--disable_host_rewrite))
- `headers` (Block List) Headers. List of (key, value) headers (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--simple_route--headers))
- `host_rewrite` (String) Host Rewrite Value. Host header will be swapped with this value
- `http_method` (String) HTTP Method. Specifies the HTTP method used to access a resource. Any HTTP Method. Possible values include `ANY`, `GET`, `HEAD`, `POST`, `PUT`, `DELETE`, `CONNECT`, `OPTIONS`, `TRACE`, `PATCH`, and others.
- `incoming_port` (Block, Optional) Port to Match. Port match of the request can be a range or a specific port (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--simple_route--incoming_port))
- `origin_pools` (Block List) Origin Pools. Origin Pools for this route (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--simple_route--origin_pools))
- `path` (Block, Optional) Path to Match. Path match of the URI can be either be, Prefix match or exact match or regular expression match (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--simple_route--path))
- `query_params` (Block, Optional) Query Parameters. Handling of incoming query parameters in simple route. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--simple_route--query_params))

<a id="nestedblock--routes--simple_route--advanced_options"></a>
### Nested Schema for `routes.simple_route.advanced_options`

Optional:

- `app_firewall` (Block, Optional) Object reference. This type establishes a direct reference from one object(the referrer) to another(the referred). Such a reference is in form of tenant/namespace/name (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--simple_route--advanced_options--app_firewall))
- `bot_defense_javascript_injection` (Block, Optional) Bot Defense Javascript Injection Configuration for inline deployments. Bot Defense Javascript Injection Configuration for inline bot defense deployments (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--simple_route--advanced_options--bot_defense_javascript_injection))
- `buffer_policy` (Block, Optional) Buffer Configuration. Some upstream applications are not capable of handling streamed data. This config enables buffering the entire request before sending to upstream application. We can specify the maximum buffer size and buffer interval with this config. Buffering can be enabled and disabled at VirtualHost and Route levels Route level buffer configuration takes precedence. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--simple_route--advanced_options--buffer_policy))
- `common_buffering` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--simple_route--advanced_options--common_buffering))
- `common_hash_policy` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--simple_route--advanced_options--common_hash_policy))
- `cors_policy` (Block, Optional) CORS Policy. Cross-Origin Resource Sharing requests configuration specified at Virtual-host or Route level. Route level configuration takes precedence. An example of an Cross origin HTTP request GET /resources/public-data/ HTTP/1.1 Host: bar.other User-Agent: Mozilla/5.0 (Macintosh; U; Intel Mac OS X 10.5; en-US; rv:1.9.1b3pre) Gecko/20081130 Minefield/3.1b3pre Accept: text/html,application/xhtml+xml,application/xml;q=0.9,*/*;q=0.8 Accept-Language: en-us,en;q=0.5 Accept-Encoding: gzip,deflate... (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--simple_route--advanced_options--cors_policy))
- `csrf_policy` (Block, Optional) CSRF Policy. To mitigate CSRF attack , the policy checks where a request is coming from to determine if the request's origin is the same as its detination.The policy relies on two pieces of information used in determining if a request originated from the same host. 1. The origin that caused the user agent to issue the request (source origin). 2. The origin that the request is going to (target origin). When the policy evaluating a request, it ensures both pieces of information are present and ... (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--simple_route--advanced_options--csrf_policy))
- `default_retry_policy` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--simple_route--advanced_options--default_retry_policy))
- `disable_location_add` (Boolean) Disable Location Addition. disables append of x-volterra-location = <re-site-name> at route level, if it is configured at virtual-host level. This configuration is ignored on CE sites.
- `disable_mirroring` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--simple_route--advanced_options--disable_mirroring))
- `disable_prefix_rewrite` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--simple_route--advanced_options--disable_prefix_rewrite))
- `disable_spdy` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--simple_route--advanced_options--disable_spdy))
- `disable_waf` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--simple_route--advanced_options--disable_waf))
- `disable_web_socket_config` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--simple_route--advanced_options--disable_web_socket_config))
- `do_not_retract_cluster` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--simple_route--advanced_options--do_not_retract_cluster))
- `enable_spdy` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--simple_route--advanced_options--enable_spdy))
- `endpoint_subsets` (Block, Optional) Origin Servers Subsets. Upstream origin pool may be configured to divide its origin servers into subsets based on metadata attached to the origin servers. Routes may then specify the metadata that a endpoint must match in order to be selected by the load balancer For origin servers which are discovered in K8S or Consul cluster, the label of the service is merged with endpoint's labels. In case of Consul, the label is derived from the 'Tag' field. For labels that are common between configured ... (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--simple_route--advanced_options--endpoint_subsets))
- `inherited_bot_defense_javascript_injection` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--simple_route--advanced_options--inherited_bot_defense_javascript_injection))
- `inherited_waf` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--simple_route--advanced_options--inherited_waf))
- `inherited_waf_exclusion` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--simple_route--advanced_options--inherited_waf_exclusion))
- `mirror_policy` (Block, Optional) Mirror Policy. MirrorPolicy is used for shadowing traffic from one origin pool to another. The approach used is 'fire and forget', meaning it will not wait for the shadow origin pool to respond before returning the response from the primary origin pool. All normal statistics are collected for the shadow origin pool making this feature useful for testing and troubleshooting. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--simple_route--advanced_options--mirror_policy))
- `no_retry_policy` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--simple_route--advanced_options--no_retry_policy))
- `prefix_rewrite` (String) Enable Prefix Rewrite. prefix_rewrite indicates that during forwarding, the matched prefix (or path) should be swapped with its value. When using regex path matching, the entire path (not including the query string) will be swapped with this value.
- `priority` (String) Routing Priority. Priority routing for each request. Different connection pools are used based on the priority selected for the request. Also, circuit-breaker configuration at destination cluster is chosen based on selected priority. Default routing mechanism High-Priority routing mechanism. Possible values are `DEFAULT`, `HIGH`.
- `regex_rewrite` (Block, Optional) Regex Match Rewrite. RegexMatchRewrite describes how to match a string and then produce a new string using a regular expression and a substitution string. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--simple_route--advanced_options--regex_rewrite))
- `request_cookies_to_add` (Block List) Add Cookies in Cookie Header. Cookies are key-value pairs to be added to HTTP request being routed towards upstream. Cookies specified at this level are applied after cookies from matched Route are applied (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--simple_route--advanced_options--request_cookies_to_add))
- `request_cookies_to_remove` (List of String) Remove Cookies from Cookie Header. List of keys of Cookies to be removed from the HTTP request being sent towards upstream.
- `request_headers_to_add` (Block List) Add Request Headers. Headers are key-value pairs to be added to HTTP request being routed towards upstream. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--simple_route--advanced_options--request_headers_to_add))
- `request_headers_to_remove` (List of String) Remove Request Headers. List of keys of Headers to be removed from the HTTP request being sent towards upstream.
- `response_cookies_to_add` (Block List) Add Set-Cookie Headers. Cookies are name-value pairs along with optional attribute parameters to be added to HTTP response being sent towards downstream. Cookies specified at this level are applied after cookies from matched Route are applied (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--simple_route--advanced_options--response_cookies_to_add))
- `response_cookies_to_remove` (List of String) Remove Cookies from Set-Cookie Headers. List of name of Cookies to be removed from the HTTP response being sent towards downstream. Entire set-cookie header will be removed
- `response_headers_to_add` (Block List) Add Response Headers. Headers are key-value pairs to be added to HTTP response being sent towards downstream. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--simple_route--advanced_options--response_headers_to_add))
- `response_headers_to_remove` (List of String) Remove Response Headers. List of keys of Headers to be removed from the HTTP response being sent towards downstream.
- `retract_cluster` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--simple_route--advanced_options--retract_cluster))
- `retry_policy` (Block, Optional) Retry Policy. Retry policy configuration for route destination. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--simple_route--advanced_options--retry_policy))
- `specific_hash_policy` (Block, Optional) Hash Policy List. List of hash policy rules (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--simple_route--advanced_options--specific_hash_policy))
- `timeout` (Number) Timeout. The timeout for the route including all retries, in milliseconds. Should be set to a high value or 0 (infinite timeout) for server-side streaming.
- `waf_exclusion_policy` (Block, Optional) Object reference. This type establishes a direct reference from one object(the referrer) to another(the referred). Such a reference is in form of tenant/namespace/name (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--simple_route--advanced_options--waf_exclusion_policy))
- `web_socket_config` (Block, Optional) Websocket Configuration. Configuration to allow Websocket Request headers of such upgrade looks like below 'connection', 'Upgrade' 'upgrade', 'websocket' With configuration to allow websocket upgrade, ADC will produce following response 'HTTP/1.1 101 Switching Protocols 'Upgrade': 'websocket' 'Connection': 'Upgrade' (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--simple_route--advanced_options--web_socket_config))

<a id="nestedblock--routes--simple_route--headers"></a>
### Nested Schema for `routes.simple_route.headers`

Optional:

- `exact` (String) Exact. Header value to match exactly
- `invert_match` (Boolean) NOT of match. Invert the result of the match to detect missing header or non-matching value
- `name` (String) Name. Name of the header
- `presence` (Boolean) Presence. If true, check for presence of header
- `regex` (String) Regex. Regex match of the header value in re2 format

- `port` (Number) Port. Exact Port to match
- `port_ranges` (String) Port range. Port range to match

<a id="nestedblock--routes--simple_route--origin_pools"></a>
### Nested Schema for `routes.simple_route.origin_pools`

Optional:

- `cluster` (Block, Optional) Object reference. This type establishes a direct reference from one object(the referrer) to another(the referred). Such a reference is in form of tenant/namespace/name (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--simple_route--origin_pools--cluster))
- `endpoint_subsets` (Block, Optional) Origin Servers Subsets. Upstream origin pool may be configured to divide its origin servers into subsets based on metadata attached to the origin servers. Routes may then specify the metadata that a endpoint must match in order to be selected by the load balancer For origin servers which are discovered in K8S or Consul cluster, the label of the service is merged with endpoint's labels. In case of Consul, the label is derived from the 'Tag' field. For labels that are common between configured ... (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--simple_route--origin_pools--endpoint_subsets))
- `pool` (Block, Optional) Object reference. This type establishes a direct reference from one object(the referrer) to another(the referred). Such a reference is in form of tenant/namespace/name (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--routes--simple_route--origin_pools--pool))
- `priority` (Number) Priority. Priority of this origin pool, valid only with multiple origin pools. Value of 0 will make the pool as lowest priority origin pool Priority of 1 means highest priority and is considered active. When active origin pool is not available, lower priority origin pools are made active as per the increasing priority.
- `weight` (Number) Weight. Weight of this origin pool, valid only with multiple origin pool. Value of 0 will disable the pool

<a id="nestedblock--sensitive_data_disclosure_rules--sensitive_data_types_in_response--body"></a>
### Nested Schema for `sensitive_data_disclosure_rules.sensitive_data_types_in_response.body`

Optional:

Optional:

- `namespace` (String) Namespace. When a configuration object(e.g. virtual_host) refers to another(e.g route) then namespace will hold the referred object's(e.g. route's) namespace.
- `tenant` (String) Tenant. When a configuration object(e.g. virtual_host) refers to another(e.g route) then tenant will hold the referred object's(e.g. route's) tenant.

<a id="nestedblock--single_lb_app--enable_malicious_user_detection"></a>
### Nested Schema for `single_lb_app.enable_malicious_user_detection`



<a id="nestedblock--slow_ddos_mitigation"></a>
### Nested Schema for `slow_ddos_mitigation`

Optional:

- `disable_request_timeout` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--slow_ddos_mitigation--disable_request_timeout))
- `request_headers_timeout` (Number) Request Headers Timeout. The amount of time the client has to send only the headers on the request stream before the stream is cancelled. The default value is 10000 milliseconds. This setting provides protection against Slowloris attacks.
- `request_timeout` (Number) Custom Timeout.

<a id="nestedblock--slow_ddos_mitigation--disable_request_timeout"></a>
### Nested Schema for `slow_ddos_mitigation.disable_request_timeout`



<a id="nestedblock--source_ip_stickiness"></a>
### Nested Schema for `source_ip_stickiness`


<a id="nestedblock--system_default_timeouts"></a>
### Nested Schema for `system_default_timeouts`


<a id="nestedblock--timeouts"></a>
### Nested Schema for `timeouts`

Optional:

- `create` (String) A string that can be [parsed as a duration](https://pkg.go.dev/time#ParseDuration) consisting of numbers and unit suffixes, such as "30s" or "2h45m". Valid time units are "s" (seconds), "m" (minutes), "h" (hours).
- `delete` (String) A string that can be [parsed as a duration](https://pkg.go.dev/time#ParseDuration) consisting of numbers and unit suffixes, such as "30s" or "2h45m". Valid time units are "s" (seconds), "m" (minutes), "h" (hours). Setting a timeout for a Delete operation is only applicable if changes are saved into state before the destroy operation occurs.
- `read` (String) A string that can be [parsed as a duration](https://pkg.go.dev/time#ParseDuration) consisting of numbers and unit suffixes, such as "30s" or "2h45m". Valid time units are "s" (seconds), "m" (minutes), "h" (hours). Read operations occur during any refresh or planning operation when refresh is enabled.
- `update` (String) A string that can be [parsed as a duration](https://pkg.go.dev/time#ParseDuration) consisting of numbers and unit suffixes, such as "30s" or "2h45m". Valid time units are "s" (seconds), "m" (minutes), "h" (hours).


<a id="nestedblock--trusted_clients"></a>
### Nested Schema for `trusted_clients`

Optional:

- `actions` (List of String) Actions. Actions that should be taken when client identifier matches the rule
- `as_number` (Number) AS Number. RFC 6793 defined 4-byte AS number
- `bot_skip_processing` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--trusted_clients--bot_skip_processing))
- `expiration_timestamp` (String) Expiration Timestamp. The expiration_timestamp is the RFC 3339 format timestamp at which the containing rule is considered to be logically expired. The rule continues to exist in the configuration but is not applied anymore.
- `http_header` (Block, Optional) HTTP Header. Request header name and value pairs (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--trusted_clients--http_header))
- `ip_prefix` (String) IPv4 Prefix. IPv4 prefix string.
- `ipv6_prefix` (String) IPv6 Prefix. IPv6 prefix string.
- `metadata` (Block, Optional) Message Metadata. MessageMetaType is metadata (common attributes) of a message that only certain messages have. This information is propagated to the metadata of a child object that gets created from the containing message during view processing. The information in this type can be specified by user during create and replace APIs. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--trusted_clients--metadata))
- `skip_processing` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--trusted_clients--skip_processing))
- `user_identifier` (String) User Identifier. Identify user based on user identifier. User identifier value needs to be copied from security event.
- `waf_skip_processing` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--trusted_clients--waf_skip_processing))

<a id="nestedblock--trusted_clients--bot_skip_processing"></a>
### Nested Schema for `trusted_clients.bot_skip_processing`


<a id="nestedblock--trusted_clients--http_header"></a>
### Nested Schema for `trusted_clients.http_header`

Optional:

- `headers` (Block List) HTTP Headers. List of HTTP header name and value pairs (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--trusted_clients--http_header--headers))

<a id="nestedblock--trusted_clients--http_header--headers"></a>
### Nested Schema for `trusted_clients.http_header.headers`

Optional:

- `exact` (String) Exact. Header value to match exactly
- `invert_match` (Boolean) NOT of match. Invert the result of the match to detect missing header or non-matching value
- `name` (String) Name. Name of the header
- `presence` (Boolean) Presence. If true, check for presence of header
- `regex` (String) Regex. Regex match of the header value in re2 format



<a id="nestedblock--trusted_clients--metadata"></a>
### Nested Schema for `trusted_clients.metadata`

Optional:

- `description` (String) Description. Human readable description.
- `name` (String) Name. This is the name of the message. The value of name has to follow DNS-1035 format.


<a id="nestedblock--trusted_clients--skip_processing"></a>
### Nested Schema for `trusted_clients.skip_processing`


<a id="nestedblock--trusted_clients--waf_skip_processing"></a>
### Nested Schema for `trusted_clients.waf_skip_processing`



<a id="nestedblock--user_id_client_ip"></a>
### Nested Schema for `user_id_client_ip`


<a id="nestedblock--user_identification"></a>
### Nested Schema for `user_identification`

Optional:

- `name` (String) Name. When a configuration object(e.g. virtual_host) refers to another(e.g route) then name will hold the referred object's(e.g. route's) name.
- `namespace` (String) Namespace. When a configuration object(e.g. virtual_host) refers to another(e.g route) then namespace will hold the referred object's(e.g. route's) namespace.
- `tenant` (String) Tenant. When a configuration object(e.g. virtual_host) refers to another(e.g route) then tenant will hold the referred object's(e.g. route's) tenant.


<a id="nestedblock--waf_exclusion"></a>
### Nested Schema for `waf_exclusion`

Optional:

- `waf_exclusion_inline_rules` (Block, Optional) WAF Exclusion Inline Rules. A list of WAF exclusion rules that will be applied inline (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--waf_exclusion--waf_exclusion_inline_rules))
- `waf_exclusion_policy` (Block, Optional) Object reference. This type establishes a direct reference from one object(the referrer) to another(the referred). Such a reference is in form of tenant/namespace/name (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--waf_exclusion--waf_exclusion_policy))

<a id="nestedblock--waf_exclusion--waf_exclusion_inline_rules"></a>
### Nested Schema for `waf_exclusion.waf_exclusion_inline_rules`

Optional:

- `rules` (Block List) WAF Exclusion Rules. An ordered list of WAF Exclusions specific to this Load Balancer. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--waf_exclusion--waf_exclusion_inline_rules--rules))

<a id="nestedblock--waf_exclusion--waf_exclusion_inline_rules--rules"></a>
### Nested Schema for `waf_exclusion.waf_exclusion_inline_rules.rules`

Optional:

- `any_domain` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--waf_exclusion--waf_exclusion_inline_rules--rules--any_domain))
- `any_path` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--waf_exclusion--waf_exclusion_inline_rules--rules--any_path))
- `app_firewall_detection_control` (Block, Optional) App Firewall Detection Control. Define the list of Signature IDs, Violations, Attack Types and Bot Names that should be excluded from triggering on the defined match criteria. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--waf_exclusion--waf_exclusion_inline_rules--rules--app_firewall_detection_control))
- `exact_value` (String) Exact Value. Exact domain name
- `expiration_timestamp` (String) Expiration Timestamp. The expiration_timestamp is the RFC 3339 format timestamp at which the containing rule is considered to be logically expired. The rule continues to exist in the configuration but is not applied anymore.
- `metadata` (Block, Optional) Message Metadata. MessageMetaType is metadata (common attributes) of a message that only certain messages have. This information is propagated to the metadata of a child object that gets created from the containing message during view processing. The information in this type can be specified by user during create and replace APIs. (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--waf_exclusion--waf_exclusion_inline_rules--rules--metadata))
- `methods` (List of String) Methods. methods to be matched
- `path_prefix` (String) Prefix. Path prefix to match (e.g. the value / will match on all paths)
- `path_regex` (String) Path Regex. Define the regex for the path. For example, the regex ^/.*$ will match on all paths
- `suffix_value` (String) Suffix Value. Suffix of domain name e.g 'xyz.com' will match '*.xyz.com' and 'xyz.com'
- `waf_skip_processing` (Block, Optional) Empty. This can be used for messages where no values are needed (see [below for nested schema](#nestedblock--waf_exclusion--waf_exclusion_inline_rules--rules--waf_skip_processing))

<a id="nestedblock--waf_exclusion--waf_exclusion_inline_rules--rules--any_domain"></a>
### Nested Schema for `waf_exclusion.waf_exclusion_inline_rules.rules.any_domain`


<a id="nestedblock--waf_exclusion--waf_exclusion_inline_rules--rules--any_path"></a>
### Nested Schema for `waf_exclusion.waf_exclusion_inline_rules.rules.any_path`


<a id="nestedblock--waf_exclusion--waf_exclusion_inline_rules--rules--app_firewall_detection_control"></a>
### Nested Schema for `waf_exclusion.waf_exclusion_inline_rules.rules.app_firewall_detection_control`

<a id="nestedblock--waf_exclusion--waf_exclusion_policy"></a>
### Nested Schema for `waf_exclusion.waf_exclusion_policy`

Optional:

- `name` (String) Name. When a configuration object(e.g. virtual_host) refers to another(e.g route) then name will hold the referred object's(e.g. route's) name.
- `namespace` (String) Namespace. When a configuration object(e.g. virtual_host) refers to another(e.g route) then namespace will hold the referred object's(e.g. route's) namespace.
- `tenant` (String) Tenant. When a configuration object(e.g. virtual_host) refers to another(e.g route) then tenant will hold the referred object's(e.g. route's) tenant.

## Import

Import is supported using the following syntax:

```shell
# Import using namespace/name format
terraform import f5xc_http_loadbalancer.example system/example
```
